2:60:3038:236:0:72:434:100:12:Times:12:Times:C:A data appendix is available at http://www.nber.org/data-appendix/w24209
3:61:3110:0:34:70:154:724:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:C:1.  Introduction
3:62:3126:34:22:70:540:690:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Civil wars are a common feature of the modern world. In2013, there were34ongoing civil wars,
3:63:3218:22:22:70:541:668:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:18in Asia and the Middle East,14in Africa and2in the Americas.1Some of these wars have been
3:64:3309:22:22:70:541:646:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:very protracted. An example is the conflict between the Lord’s Resistance Army and the Ugandan
3:65:3403:22:22:70:541:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:state, which can be traced back to1987or the civil war in Mindanao, the southern island of the
3:66:3497:22:21:70:541:602:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Philippines,  which  has  been ongoing  since  the  late1960s  (Allen  and  Vlassenroot,2010).  These
3:67:3598:21:22:70:541:581:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:wars  cause  a  great  deal  of  damage  and  loss  of  human  life.   In2013alone,  an  estimated70,451
3:68:3702:22:22:70:541:559:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:people died fighting in civil wars and10.7million civilians were newly displaced, resulting in a
3:69:3798:22:22:70:380:537:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:total stock of33million people being displaced due to conflict.2
3:70:3862:22:22:85:541:515:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In  this  paper,  we  test  a  long-standing  hypothesis  from  the  field  of  anthropology  about  the
3:71:3966:22:22:70:541:493:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relationship  between  conflict  and  the  kinship  structure  of  a  society,  namely  whether  an  ethnic
3:72:4073:22:22:70:541:471:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:group is organized into segmentary lineages.  Although in Western cultures, the central kinship
3:73:4168:22:22:70:541:449:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:unit  is  the  nuclear  family,  in  most  of  the  world  people  live  within  much  more  complex  social
3:74:4276:22:22:70:541:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:structures, connected by extended kin networks. Segmentary lineage is one such social structure.
3:75:4372:22:22:70:541:405:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The first defining characteristic of this organizational form is unilineal descent, where people trace
3:76:4474:22:22:70:541:383:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:their  ancestry  back  either  through  either  the  male  line  (patrilineal)  or  female  line  (matrilineal),
3:77:4586:22:22:70:541:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:but not both. Typically, ancestry is traced back to a common, often mythical, founder, after whom
3:78:4683:22:22:70:541:339:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the tribe or society is named.  Examples areSamaleandOrmawho are the common ancestors of
3:79:4771:22:21:70:541:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the Somali and Oromo (Ahmed,2013b, p.20).  The second feature is the presence of sub-sets or
3:80:4863:21:22:70:540:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segments of a full lineage, which function as coherent autonomous groups (Smith,1956, pp.39–
3:81:4955:22:22:70:541:274:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:40). The lineage segments take a ‘corporate form,’ meaning that they are important for organizing
3:82:5052:22:22:70:541:252:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a range of activities and functions that are political, judicial, and administrative in nature (Fortes,
3:83:5155:22:22:70:103:230:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:C:1953).3
3:84:5162:22:22:85:541:208:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Figure1displays a hypothetical patrilineal segmentary lineage system. In the figure, triangles
3:85:5256:22:22:70:541:186:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:indicate  men  and  the  straight  lines  indicate  descent,  with  each  row  of  triangles  indicating  a
3:86:5363:22:22:70:541:164:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:generation. All individuals in the figure descend from a common ancestor indicated by “I.” Also
3:87:5458:22:19:70:541:142:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:shown in the figure are various segments of the full lineage.  The segments are of different sizes:
3:88:5557:19:13:83:488:123:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:1These figures are based on the authors’ calculations using the UCDP/PRIO Armed Conflict Dataset.
3:89:5654:13:13:83:516:110:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:2These figures are from the UCDP Battle-Related Deaths Dataset and the UNHCR Statistical Yearbook,2013.
3:90:5757:13:14:83:541:97:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:3As  described  by  Fortes  (1953,  p.26):  “the  individual  has  no  legal  or  political  status  except  as  a  member  of  a
3:91:5886:14:11:70:541:83:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:lineage;. . . all legal and political relations in the society take place in the context of the lineage system. . . all the members
3:92:6017:11:11:70:541:72:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:of a lineage are to outsiders jurally equal and represent the lineage when they exercise legal and political rights and
3:93:6136:11:0:70:416:61:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:duties in relation to society at large. This is what underlies. . . collective responsibility.”
4:94:6232:0:17:258:355:706:6:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f7:F:MaximalLineage
4:95:6246:17:61:305:309:689:6:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f8:F:I
4:96:6247:61:29:169:256:628:6:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f7:F:Major Segment
4:97:6260:29:19:211:407:599:6:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f8:F:AB
4:98:6262:19:11:148:183:580:6:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f7:F:Minor
4:99:6267:11:28:141:189:569:6:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f7:F:Segment
4:100:6274:28:50:166:453:541:6:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f8:F:1234
4:101:6278:50:13:142:477:491:6:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f8:F:abcdefgh
4:102:6286:13:15:118:165:478:6:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f7:F:Minimal
4:103:6293:15:28:118:166:463:6:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f7:F:Segment
4:104:6300:28:23:128:490:435:6:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f8:F:iiiiiiivvviviiviiiixxxixiixiiixivxvxvi
4:105:6339:23:47:82:530:412:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Figure1:   The figure provides a representation of a hypothetical segmentary lineage society.
4:106:6432:47:22:70:541:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The smallest is the “Minimal Segment,” the next larger is the “Minor Segment,” and the largest
4:107:6526:22:22:70:187:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is the “Major Segment.”
4:108:6549:22:22:85:541:321:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Although  it  is  true  that,  from  a  biological  perspective,  decent  is  universal  among  human
4:109:6650:22:21:70:541:299:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:societies, in terms of social significance, descent varies significantly.  For example, not all groups
4:110:6752:21:22:70:541:278:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:trace  descent  through  unilineal  lineages.   Another  common  kinship  form  is  cognatic  descent
4:111:6853:22:22:70:541:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:where individuals can simultaneously belong to two sets of groups and trace their lineage through
4:112:6950:22:22:70:541:234:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:either their mother’s relatives, father’s relatives, or both. Many small-scale societies, for example,
4:113:7052:22:22:70:541:212:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:hunter-gatherer groups such as the Hadza or San, have no established elaborate kinship system
4:114:7145:22:22:70:541:190:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:at all.  In addition, the importance placed on a society’s kinship system, as well as the associated
4:115:7245:22:22:70:541:168:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:responsibilities and obligations, also vary widely.  Unlike in a segmentary lineage society, where
4:116:7343:22:22:70:541:146:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  and  kinship  are  of  the  utmost  importance,  in  many  societies,  local  residence  functions
4:117:7450:22:22:70:541:124:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as a primary source of identity, even though this clearly mixes together individuals who are not
4:118:7546:22:22:70:541:102:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:genetically related.  In other societies, completely different types of social structures, such as age
4:119:7648:22:22:70:541:80:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sets  and  age  grades,  provide  the  main  way  of  organizing  societies,  both  administratively  and
4:120:7753:22:0:70:120:58:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:politically.
5:121:7766:0:22:85:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:A  number  of  scholars  in  the  anthropology  literature  have  hypothesized  that  there  is  a  rela-
5:122:7871:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tionship between the social structure of groups and the prevalence of violence and conflict. More
5:123:7968:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:specifically,  it  is  argued  that  segmentary  lineage  societies  are  more  prone  to  become  engaged
5:124:8074:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  more  conflicts,  and  in  ones  that  are  longer  in  duration  and  larger  in  scale,  than  societies
5:125:8184:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:without a segmentary lineage structure.  This is not because segmentary lineage societies harbor
5:126:8280:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:particular grievances, but because the social structure is designed to mobilize combatants when a
5:127:8377:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:dispute or conflict occurs.  To see why this is the case, consider Figure1.  An important aspect of
5:128:8476:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage societies is that lineages and segments, and one’s responsibility to them, are of
5:129:8576:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the utmost importance. In the figure, if individual “i” were to have a dispute with individual “ix”
5:130:8675:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:within a segmentary lineage system,  this would mean that all individuals belonging to “Major
5:131:8768:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Segment  A”  would  be  allied  with,  and  come  to  the  defense  of,  individual  “i.”   Similarly,  all
5:132:8875:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:individuals in “Major Segment B” would be allied with and come to the defense of individual
5:133:8966:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:“ix.”  Thus, a dispute between two individuals immediately escalates into a dispute between two
5:134:9061:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:large  communities.   Outside  of  segmentary  lineage  systems,  these  allegiances  do  not  exist  and
5:135:9166:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the dispute might comprise,  at most,  a small number of friends or family members of the two
5:136:9259:22:22:70:185:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:involved in the dispute.
5:137:9283:22:22:85:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:More generally, the number of individuals involved in a conflict depends on the genealogical
5:138:9375:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:distance of those involved in the dispute. Because of one’s membership in a set of nested segments
5:139:9473:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and the strong obligations to one’s kinsmen within the segments, in segmentary lineage societies,
5:140:9570:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:small-scale  disputes  can  easily  escalate  into  larger-scale,  sustained  fighting  or  even  full-blown
5:141:9678:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:warfare.  In the modern context, and particularly in Africa, the region of our study, conflict often
5:142:9778:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:takes the form of civil conflict, where the external enemy is the government. However, even in this
5:143:9877:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:context, the same characteristics of segmentary lineage societies are still relevant.  The structure
5:144:9977:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:allows segments to effectively mobilize against the common enemy, which in the setting of civil
5:145:10072:22:22:70:182:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:war is the government.
5:146:10094:22:22:85:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:This  characteristic  of  segmentary  lineage  systems  has  been  well-studied  by  anthropologists.
5:147:10195:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:For  example,  Sahlins  (1961,  pp.323,333)  argues  that  “segmentary  lineage  organization  is  a
5:148:10295:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:successful  predatory  organization  in  conflicts  with  other  tribes. . . [Conflict],  even  if  it  has  been
5:149:10408:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:initiated by a small lineage segment, it pits ‘all of us’ against ‘them’." Along similar lines, Evans-
5:150:10510:22:22:70:541:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Pritchard  (1940a,  p.142)  describes  the  organization  of  the  Nuer,  a  segmentary  lineage  group:
5:151:10614:22:0:70:541:66:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:“Each segment is itself segmented and there is opposition between its parts. The members of any
6:152:10710:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segment unite for war against adjacent segments of the same order and unite with these adjacent
6:153:10805:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segments against larger sections.”  The logic is also illustrated by a traditional Bedouin proverb
6:154:10903:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that is roughly translated as:  “I against my brothers; my brothers and I against my cousins; my
6:155:10999:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cousins, my brothers, and I against the world.” (e.g., Barth,1973, p.13; Combs-Schilling,1985, p.
6:156:11096:22:22:70:93:636:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:660).
6:157:11101:22:22:85:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In  this  study,  we  take  this  long-standing  hypothesis  to  the  data  and  test  for  a  relationship
6:158:11208:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:between the presence of segmentary lineage organization and conflict today. There are a number
6:159:11302:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of benefits to moving beyond the case study evidence.  First, it is unclear whether the cases that
6:160:11400:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:have  been  examined  in  the  anthropology  literature  are  a  representative  sample  of  all  possible
6:161:11506:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cases.    Our  empirical  strategy  has  the  advantage  of  being  able  to  estimate  an  average  effect
6:162:11613:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:across ethnicities in our sample.  Second, it is possible that segmentary lineages, exactly because
6:163:11712:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:they  escalate  the  scale  of  conflict  if  it  starts,  prevent  wars  from  occurring.   In  other  words,  in
6:164:11826:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:theory,  segmentary  lineage  societies  may  escalate  conflicts  if  they  start,  but  also  prevent  them
6:165:11935:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from starting in the first place.  The case-study literature provides no evidence of this.  However,
6:166:12035:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a  lack  of  evidence  for  this  channel  is  not  the  same  as  evidence  against  such  a  channel.   Our
6:167:12144:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:empirical analysis allows us to estimate the separate effects of segmentary lineage organization
6:168:12240:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and conflict onset and on conflict escalation.  Third, the ethnographic studies are primarily from
6:169:12338:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:before the1970s and so it is possible that the strength of segmentary lineage organization, and the
6:170:12437:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:obligations that go with it, have weakened in recent decades. Although, there are many examples
6:171:12532:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of segmentary lineages between important for recruitment in modern conflicts (e.g., Sterns,2013),
6:172:12629:22:22:70:449:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our findings will provide systematic evidence that is relevant to this question.
6:173:12709:22:21:85:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Information  on  the  presence  of  segmentary  lineage  systems  is  not  available  from  standard
6:174:12809:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ethnographic sources such as theEthnographic Atlasor theStandard Cross-Cultural Sample.  There-
6:175:12904:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fore, we collected data using previously published ethnographies.  The primary source used was
6:176:12998:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:theEthnographic Survey of Africa, which is a series of studies, produced from the1940s until the
6:177:13094:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:1970s and edited by Daryll Forde. Following the definition of Middleton and Tait (1958), we define
6:178:13192:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an  ethnic  group  as  having  a  segmentary  lineage  organization  if:  (1)  there  is  a  recognized  and
6:179:13300:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:known unilineal descent system; (2) segments of the lineage take a ‘corporate form’, meaning that
6:180:13397:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:they are sub-units that are important and affect administrative functions and political positions.;
6:181:13496:22:22:70:541:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and (3) lineages and genealogical relationships influence one’s location of residence.  We code an
6:182:13594:22:0:70:541:66:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ethnicity as not having a segmentary lineage organization if any of these three characteristics are
7:183:13694:0:22:70:191:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:known to not be present.
7:184:13718:22:22:85:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We restricted our data collection to ethnic groups from Africa. This was done for two reasons.
7:185:13812:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:First, the ethnographic data are most readily available from comparable and systematically doc-
7:186:13907:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:umented sources for groups within Africa. Second, and probably most important, the geo-coded
7:187:13999:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:micro-level conflict data that we use (described below) is only available for Africa.  In the end,
7:188:14097:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we  are  able  to  definitively  categorize145African  ethnic  groups,74of  which  are  segmentary
7:189:14195:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  societies  and71of  which  are  not.   Although  we  are  unable  to  construct  measures  for
7:190:14298:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:every  ethnic  group  within  Africa,  our  sample  is  sizeable,  comprising  an  estimated212million
7:191:14400:22:21:70:412:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:people or approximately 38% of the population of sub-Saharan Africa.
7:192:14468:21:22:85:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We  use  conflict  data  from  the  Armed  Conflict  Location  and  Event  Data  Project  (ACLED),  a
7:193:14569:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:geo-coded  data  set  that  catalogs  information  about  each  conflict  event  in  Africa  from  January
7:194:14675:22:22:70:540:483:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:1,1997to  December31,2014.   The  database  includes  information  on  the  location,  date,  and
7:195:14772:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:other characteristics of “politically violent events.”4To link the conflict data with the data on the
7:196:14873:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage structure of each ethnic group,  we use the digitized map of the traditional locations of
7:197:14970:22:22:70:540:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ethnic groups from Murdock (1959) to calculate the frequency of conflicts that occur within the
7:198:15065:22:22:70:221:395:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:territory of each ethnic group.5
7:199:15097:22:22:85:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our  empirical  analysis  comprises  two  estimation  strategies.The  first  is  to  estimate  the
7:200:15195:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cross-ethnicity relationship between the traditional presence of a segmentary lineage organization
7:201:15293:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and the prevalence of conflicts from1997–2014.  Our estimates show a positive and statistically
7:202:15388:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:significant relationship between segmentary lineage and a range of conflict measures, including
7:203:15483:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict  incidence,  duration,  and  fatalities.   In  addition,  we  also  examine  conflicts  of  different
7:204:15593:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:types – namely, civil conflicts, non-civil conflicts, and localized within-group conflicts.  We find
7:205:15693:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  that  segmentary  lineage  experience  more  of  each  type  of  conflict.   In  addition,  to  being
7:206:15800:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:statistically  significant,  the  estimated  effects  are  also  quantitatively  meaningful.   For  example,
7:207:15908:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:according to our estimates, segmentary lineage societies experienced approximately 100% more
7:208:16000:22:22:70:431:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:deadly conflict incidents relative to societies without segmentary lineages.
7:209:16076:22:20:85:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We  find  that  these  relationships  are  robust  to  controlling  for  a  large  number  of  covariates,
7:210:16182:20:14:83:541:134:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:4Civil  conflicts  (i.e.,  conflicts  between  the  government  military  and  other  non-government  groups)  account  for
7:211:16305:14:11:70:541:120:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:39.4% of the117,823events in their database, while the other60.6% are non-civil-conflict events that do not involve the
7:212:16424:11:9:70:154:109:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:government military.
7:213:16444:9:15:83:541:100:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:5The strategy of using location to link conflicts to ethnic groups follows the methodology of Michalopoulos and
7:214:16555:15:10:70:540:85:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:Papaioannou (2016).  Prior to this, the same methodology was also used to estimate average incomes of ethnic groups
7:215:16670:10:0:70:469:75:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:(e.g., Michalopoulos and Papaioannou,2013,2014, Alesina, Michalopoulos and Papaioannou,2016).
8:216:16764:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:including:  country fixed effects, historical covariates (namely, political centralization and histor-
8:217:16866:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ical  development  as  measured  by  settlement  complexity),  and  a  host  of  geographic  covariates
8:218:16969:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(agricultural  suitability,  altitude,  distance  from  the  equator,  amount  of  land  inhabited  by  the
8:219:17076:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ethnic group, distance from the center of an ethnic group to the nearest country border, and an
8:220:17171:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:indicator for the ethnic group being split by a national border). The estimates of interest are very
8:221:17271:22:22:70:343:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:similar whether or not we condition on these covariates.
8:222:17327:22:22:85:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The conditional correlations potentially suffer from the standard inference issues that plague
8:223:17421:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cross-sectional  estimates,  namely  the  presence  of  omitted  factors,  particularly  those  that  are
8:224:17526:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:unobservable  to  the  researcher.   Given  this,  we  implement  a  second  set  of  estimates  that  at-
8:225:17632:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tempt  to  address  the  presence  of  omitted  factors  that  may  bias  our  estimates.   We  first  restrict
8:226:17743:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:attention to pairs of ethnic groups that share a border and where one has a segmentary lineage
8:227:17837:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization  and  the  other  does  not.   In  our  sample,  there  are68such  pairs.   We  then  take
8:228:17940:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:10km-by-10km grid-cells to be the unit of observation and implement a regression discontinuity
8:229:18034:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(RD) identification strategy, where we estimate the effect of segmentary lineage organization on
8:230:18130:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict across grid-cells that are restricted to be sufficiently close to the border, while controlling
8:231:18234:22:22:70:260:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for two-dimensional running variables.
8:232:18272:22:22:85:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We find that the RD estimates are qualitatively identical to our OLS estimates.  The estimated
8:233:18366:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relationships  between  segmentary  lineage  organization  and  conflict  are  all  positive  and  highly
8:234:18471:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:significant.   These  findings  hold  for  each  of  our  measures  of  conflict,  for  a  range  of  different
8:235:18582:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:bandwidths,  and  for  a  number  of  different  specifications  that  control  for  the  two-dimensional
8:236:18687:22:22:70:158:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:running variables.
8:237:18705:22:21:85:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The benefit of the RD estimates over the OLS estimates is that omitted factors, even those that
8:238:18800:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are  unobservable,  are  better  accounted  for.   As  long  as  the  omitted  factors  vary  smoothly  over
8:239:18908:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:space – for example, because physically close units have similar geography, climate, and history –
8:240:19006:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:they will be taken into account by the RD estimation strategy. However, the strategy is ineffective
8:241:19105:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:if the omitted factors also vary discontinuously at the border. In other words, there may be other
8:242:19203:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:differences between the ethnic groups besides the presence of segmentary lineages and the RD
8:243:19295:22:22:70:327:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates may be capturing these differences as well.
8:244:19348:22:22:85:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:To explore the potential importance of this issue, we first check average differences in observ-
8:245:19444:22:22:70:541:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:able characteristics between societies with and without segmentary lineages. We find that the two
8:246:19541:22:0:70:541:66:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups are balanced on a wide variety of observable covariates.  This finding is consistent with
9:247:19638:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:arguments suggesting that the presence of segmentary lineage societies is not correlated with a
9:248:19733:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:large set of structural factors, but is an idiosyncratic process (Evans-Pritchard and Fortes,1940,
9:249:19831:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Smith,1956, Salzman,1978, Kelly,1983).  Second, we conduct a series of placebo tests where we
9:250:19924:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:classify ethnic groups as either treatment or control based on a range of alternative ethnicity-level
9:251:20025:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:characteristics.   We  then  use  our  RD  specification  to  estimate  any  treatment  effects  for  these
9:252:20132:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:alternative  characteristics.   To  make  sure  that  any  observed  effect  is  not  driven  by  segmentary
9:253:20240:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage organization, for the placebo checks, we focus the comparison on ethnicity pairs with the
9:254:20337:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:same segmentary lineage classification. Reassuringly, we find no statistically significant effects of
9:255:20438:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:these other characteristics on conflict.  Importantly, the point estimates are not only statistically
9:256:20539:21:22:70:272:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:insignificant but also small in magnitude.
9:257:20581:22:22:85:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:One of the conditions that is necessary for the validity of the RD estimates is that we correctly
9:258:20678:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:identify  the  location  of  ethnic  boundaries.   We  check  whether  this  is  satisfied  using  data  from
9:259:20787:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the third round of the Afrobarometer surveys on the location and ethnicity of over5,500respon-
9:260:20881:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:dents.   The  RD  estimate,  with  self-reported  ethnicity  as  the  outcome  variable,  shows  a  sharp
9:261:20986:22:22:70:534:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:discontinuity at ethnicity borders. This provides confidence in the validity of our RD estimates.
9:262:21083:22:22:85:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  primary  mechanism  explaining  the  estimated  relationship  between  segmentary  lineage
9:263:21178:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:societies and conflict is the strong in-group allegiances and segmented structure that can cause
9:264:21274:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:initially-small  disputes  to  escalate  into  larger-scale  conflicts.   In  addition,  given  these  effects,
9:265:21385:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary  lineage  organization  could,  in  theory,  actually  result  in  fewer  conflicts.   It  may  be
9:266:21494:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  conflicts  tend  to  be  larger  in  scale  and  duration  if  they  occur,  but  are  less  likely  to  occur.
9:267:21611:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We explore these and related issues by separately estimating the effects of segmentary lineage on
9:268:21708:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the onset of new conflicts and on the duration (i.e., offset) of existing conflicts.  Estimating these
9:269:21810:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:two mechanisms using a set of hazard models, we find that the presence of a segmentary lineage
9:270:21904:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization  increases  the  duration  of  conflicts.   This  effect  is  large  in  magnitude  and  highly
9:271:22012:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:significant.  Turning to conflict onset, we find that segmentary lineage also has a positive effect,
9:272:22112:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:although it is smaller in magnitude and less precisely estimated.  Thus, there is no evidence that
9:273:22210:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage organization, through its escalation effects, prevents conflicts from occurring
9:274:22308:22:22:70:151:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the first place.
9:275:22327:22:22:85:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:As an alternative method to examine the escalation effect of segmentary lineages, we estimate
9:276:22420:22:22:70:541:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  relationship  between  a  segmentary  lineage  organization  and  the  frequency  of  conflicts  of
9:277:22524:22:0:70:541:66:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:different  sizes,  namely  conflicts  with:   no  fatalities,1–10fatalities,11–100fatalities,  and  more
10:278:22629:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:than100fatalities.  We find that although segmentary lineage organization is associated with a
10:279:22723:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:greater  probability  of  conflicts  of  all  types,  the  estimated  relationship  is  significantly  stronger,
10:280:22835:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:both in terms of magnitude and statistical significance, the larger the conflict.  In addition, these
10:281:22936:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:differences are large. For example, we find that while segmentary lineage societies have59% more
10:282:23032:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflicts with zero fatalities, they have183% more conflicts with over100fatalities. These findings
10:283:23131:22:22:70:518:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are consistent with segmentary lineages working, in part, through an escalation mechanism.
10:284:23221:22:22:85:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  final  empirical  exercise  that  we  undertake  is  motivated  by  the  existing  evidence  of  the
10:285:23326:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relationship  between  adverse  rainfall  shocks  and  civil  conflict  within  sub-Saharan  Africa  (e.g.,
10:286:23433:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Miguel,  Satyanath  and  Saiegh,2004).   We  test  whether  the  effect  of  adverse  rainfall  shocks  on
10:287:23539:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict is different for segmentary lineage societies.  We find greater effects of rainfall shocks on
10:288:23641:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflicts for segmentary lineage ethnicities.  In fact, we find that the average relationship across
10:289:23741:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:all ethnicities in our sample is driven solely by segmentary lineage societies.  For ethnic groups
10:290:23839:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:without segmentary lineage organization, the relationship between adverse rainfall and conflict
10:291:23934:22:22:70:478:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is not statistically different from zero, and if anything, negative rather than positive.
10:292:24023:22:22:85:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our  findings  contribute  to  a  better  understanding  of  the  incidence,  intensity,  and  duration
10:293:24126:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of conflict in developing countries.6This literature has proposed various types of explanations,
10:294:24222:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:many  based  on  the  dichotomy  between  ‘greed’  and  ‘grievance’  (Collier  and  Sambanis,2005).
10:295:24321:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Greed factors influence whether or not individuals or groups decide to engage in civil war. These
10:296:24418:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:include  things  like  the  presence  of  ‘lootable  wealth,’  such  as  oil  or  diamonds  (Weinstein,2006,
10:297:24526:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Ross,2004,2006), or foreign aid (De Ree and Nillesen,2009, Nunn and Qian,2014, Crost, Felter
10:298:24618:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Johnston,2014). On the grievance side, conflict could be induced by inequality within society
10:299:24715:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(Cederman, Gleditsch and Buhaug,2013), the presence of ethnic cleavages (Montalvo and Reynal-
10:300:24808:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Querol,2005, Esteban, Mayoral and Ray,2012), arbitrary national boundaries (Michalopoulos and
10:301:24901:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Papaioannou,2016),  the lack of political accountability and democracy (Gleditsch and Ruggeri,
10:302:24995:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:2010)  or  other  types  of  exploitative  institutions  (Richards,1996,  Wood,2003).   Also  potentially
10:303:25100:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:important  are  factors  that  influence  the  opportunity  cost  of  engaging  in  conflict  (Miguel  et  al.,
10:304:25211:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:2004, Debos,2011, Hoffman,2011, McGovern,2011, Dube and Vargas,2013, Debos,2016). A final
10:305:25300:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:recurrent theme in the literature is that conflict – namely, civil conflict – occurs as a consequence
10:306:25401:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of state weakness, as proxied by real per capita GDP (Fearon and Laitin,2003) or measured more
10:307:25495:22:19:70:312:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:directly by state history (Depetris-Chauvin,2014).
10:308:25545:19:0:83:349:69:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:6See Blattman and Miguel (2010) for an overview of this literature.
11:309:25613:0:22:85:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our findings also contribute to a well-established anthropological literature that, through case
11:310:25709:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:studies, has hypothesized and documented the effects that segmentary lineage structures have on
11:311:25804:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict (e.g., Evans-Pritchard,1940a,b, Bohannon,1958, Kelly,1985, Lewis,1994,1989, Salzman,
11:312:25897:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:2007, Zeman,2009, Stearns,2013, Ahmed,2013b, Hoehne,2015). While the studies recognize that
11:313:25988:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage organization can potentially affect all types of conflict, their focus tends to be
11:314:26089:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on the effects that segmentary lineages have on smaller-scale within-ethnicity conflict, whether it
11:315:26188:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be individuals from the same village against one another or individuals from separate villages
11:316:26282:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:against one another.  Our estimates test for this directly by examining the effects of segmentary
11:317:26379:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage organization on localized within-group conflicts, as well as extending this line of inquiry
11:318:26478:21:22:70:455:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and asking whether the same mechanisms are also important for civil conflicts.
11:319:26556:22:22:85:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our findings also contribute to a deeper understanding of the long-run consequences of the
11:320:26646:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:pre-colonial characteristics of African societies. A number of important studies have documented
11:321:26742:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the importance of historical political centralization for economic outcomes today (e.g., Gennaioli
11:322:26840:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Rainer,2007, Michalopoulos and Papaioannou,2013).  Although this is clearly an important
11:323:26932:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:determinant of subsequent outcomes, our analysis shows that other dimensions – namely, social
11:324:27025:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:structure and the nature of kinship – are also important.  Our focus on this dimension of social
11:325:27121:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:structure connects our findings to previous studies that also examine the importance of various
11:326:27216:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:dimensions  of  social  structure  within  developing  countries.    For  example,  La  Ferrara  (2007),
11:327:27320:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Gneezy,  Leonard  and  List  (2009),  La  Ferrara  and  Milazzo  (2011)  and  Lowes  (2016)  study  the
11:328:27423:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:importance of matrilineal versus patrilineal inheritance, while Bau (2016) studies the importance
11:329:27520:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  matrilocal  versus  patrilocal  residence.   Dunning  and  Harrison  (2010)  show  how  the  social
11:330:27623:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:custom  of  cross-cutting  alliances  called  “cousinage”  influences  the  appeal  of  ethnic  political
11:331:27728:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:appeals  in  Mali.   Greif  (1994)  examines  the  institutional  divergence  between  Genoa  and  other
11:332:27832:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:parts of the Mediterranean by positing differences in underlying kinship relations, which did not
11:333:27929:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:allow the Genoese to use community enforcement mechanisms in contractual relations and Greif
11:334:28021:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Tabellini (2010),  building on a large historical literature,  use a similar argument to explain
11:335:28121:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the historical divergence between Europe and China.  More recently, studies have examined the
11:336:28214:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relationship between the strength and scope of kinship networks and democracy (Schulz,2017),
11:337:28306:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:corruption (Akbari, Bahrami-Rad and Kimbrough,2017), and cooperation and long-run economic
11:338:28396:22:22:70:198:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:development (Enke,2017).
11:339:28420:22:0:85:541:66:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The difference between attitudes towards and treatment of family members versus non-family
12:340:28511:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:members has a basis in biology (Hamilton,1963, Henrich and Henrich,2007) and has been applied
12:341:28604:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to  study  problems  of  economic  development  (Banfield,1958).    Kinship,  as  measured  by  the
12:342:28703:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:strength of family ties, has also been extensively used in the literature on social networks (Ansell
12:343:28803:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Padgett,1993, Naidu, Robinson and Young,2015), and has been shown to be associated with
12:344:28894:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a range of economic, social, and political outcomes (Alesina and Giuliano,2014).  In the political
12:345:28992:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:economy literature, family ties have also been explored as sources of political power and dynastic
12:346:29090:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:politics (Dal Bo, Dal Bo and Snyder,2009, Querubín,2016, Cruz, Labonne and Querubin,2017).
12:347:29180:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Our findings also add to the existing literature on the importance of family structure (Todd,1985).
12:348:29279:22:21:85:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  paper  proceeds  as  follows.   In  the  next  section,  we  review  the  existing  anthropological
12:349:29383:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:explanations  for  why  some  societies  are  organized  along  the  basis  of  segmentary  lineages  and
12:350:29488:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:others are not. We then discuss case study evidence which makes a causal link between segmen-
12:351:29581:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tary lineage organization and conflict.  Section3discusses the data and in particular the way in
12:352:29677:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:which  we  coded  whether  or  not  a  particular  society  has  a  segmentary  lineage  structure  based
12:353:29782:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on ethnographic sources.  Section4presents our OLS estimates, while section5presents our RD
12:354:29873:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates. Section6attempts to gain insights into mechanisms by examining onset, duration, and
12:355:29967:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the differential relationship between adverse rainfall shocks and conflict.  Section7discusses the
12:356:30065:22:40:70:496:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relevance of our findings for ethnic groups outside of Africa, while section8concludes.
12:357:30152:40:34:70:151:333:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:C:2.  Background
12:358:30166:34:30:70:485:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:A.  Descriptive Evidence of a Relationship between Segmentary Lineage and Conflict
12:359:30248:30:22:70:541:269:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Numerous studies have documented examples of an apparent link between segmentary lineage
12:360:30336:22:22:70:541:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization and the initiation and/or propagation of conflict.  Many point out the strong effect
12:361:30433:22:21:70:541:225:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  segmentary  lineage  organization  can  have  on  the  exacerbation  of  small  conflicts.   Once  a
12:362:30539:21:22:70:541:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict begins,  segmentary lineage structure results in an essentially automatic mobilization of
12:363:30637:22:22:70:436:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:additional combatants, which makes resolving the conflict much less likely.
12:364:30712:22:22:85:541:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:One  of  the  best-studied  segmentary  lineage  societies  is  the  Somali,  whose  social  structure
12:365:30814:22:22:70:541:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is  dominated  by  segmentary  organization.   Anthropologist  Ioan  Lewis  (1961)  argues  that  the
12:366:30915:22:22:70:541:116:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage system plays a major role in propagating conflict in Somalia.  He writes that
12:367:31011:22:22:70:541:94:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:“quarrels between individuals which result in loss of life or property or both are often quickly
12:368:31107:22:0:70:541:72:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:followed  by  retaliation  where  there  is  little  thought  of  negotiation.   Within  a  clan  bitter  feuds
13:369:31220:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:develop  and  persist,  often  for  many  years  and  sometimes  generations,  erupting  spasmodically
13:370:31322:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as later incidents occur, and being temporarily forgotten only in the context of wider hostilities”
13:371:31421:22:22:70:171:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(Lewis,1961, p.243).
13:372:31441:22:22:85:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Segmentary  lineage  has  also  been  associated  with  more-organized  forms  of  conflict,  like
13:373:31539:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:political  violence.    In  his  bookBlood  and  Bone,  Ioan  Lewis  (1994)  describes  the  link  between
13:374:31645:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage organization and organized violence in the Somali region during the1980s.
13:375:31737:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:After the Ogaadeen war of1977–1978, there was an upsurge of “tribalism,” which was led by the
13:376:31830:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:President Siyad, whose goal was to consolidate the position of his own clan and family.  Rather
13:377:31925:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:than develop a national identity, his strategy was to recruit as many tribal segments as possible
13:378:32022:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:within  the  segmentary  system.   In  turn,  this  caused  segments  opposed  to  the  government  to
13:379:32124:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:build allegiances among their own segments (Lewis,1994, pp.225–226). That is, the “segmentary
13:380:32217:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:structure  allowed  both  the  government  and  opposition  to  mobilize  large  swaths  of  the  lineage
13:381:32322:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:system” (Lewis,1994, p.232). This societal polarization along tribal and genealogical lines lays at
13:382:32421:22:22:70:346:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the foundation of Somalia’s subsequent political conflict.
13:383:32479:22:22:85:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Even  today,  the  relationship  between  lineage  organization  and  violent  conflict  continues  to
13:384:32581:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be  important.   A2015Rift  Valley  Institute  Report  reaffirms  its  importance  in  a  discussion  of
13:385:32685:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an upsurge of conflict during2006.  It describes how the military efforts of the Warsangeli and
13:386:32780:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Dubays fighters is “in line with the segmentary logic of the northern Somali society as a whole: as
13:387:32879:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:soon as a common threat emerges from outside, members of a descent group unite at the highest
13:388:32972:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:necessary level (sub-clan, clan or clan-family). Conversely, in the absence of such a threat, a group
13:389:33073:22:22:70:446:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:breaks up into smaller units that fend for themselves” (Hoehne,2015, p.217).
13:390:33149:22:21:85:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  Somali  example  clearly  illustrates  the  obligations  that  arise  due  to  segmentary  lineages
13:391:33253:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  how  these  can  cause  individuals  to  align  with  large  portions  of  society  against  common
13:392:33357:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:threats  and  to  become  involved  in  conflicts  even  if  they  are  otherwise  far  removed  from  the
13:393:33463:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:source  of  the  conflict.   This  effect  has  also  been  documented  among  several  other  segmentary
13:394:33568:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage groups.  The Nuer, an ethnic group from South Sudan that strictly abides by segmentary
13:395:33662:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  organization,  have  been  well  studied.  Evans-Pritchard  (1940a)  describes  this  obligation
13:396:33767:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:among the Nuer of South Sudan, writing that they “state this structural principle clearly in the
13:397:33863:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:expression of their political values. Thus they say that if the Leng tertiary section of the Lou tribe
13:398:33965:22:22:70:541:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fights the Nyarkwac tertiary section – and, in fact, there has been a long feud between them – the
13:399:34063:22:0:70:520:66:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:villages which compose each section will combine to fight.” (Evans-Pritchard,1940a, p.142).
14:400:34156:0:22:85:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Numerous other segmentary lineage societies also exhibit this same pattern.  Lienhardt (1958)
14:401:34249:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:describes this same allegiance structure among the Dinka. Bohannon (1958) describes it amongst
14:402:34343:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  Tiv  of  Nigeria,  another  segmentary  lineage  society  and  provides  the  specific  example  of
14:403:34447:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fighting  between  the  Morov  of  MbaKetsa  and  MbaHura  of  Tondov.In  this  case  also,  the
14:404:34543:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary structure facilitated recruitment to conflict, which significantly escalated a feud that
14:405:34642:22:38:70:381:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:began between just two tribal segments (Bohannon,1958, p.46).
14:406:34703:38:30:70:212:576:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:B.  Other Systems of Kinship
14:407:34731:30:22:70:541:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Those societies without segmentary lineage organization comprise our control group. A common
14:408:34823:22:22:70:541:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:alternative  organization  form  is  centered  around  the  village,  which  is  led  by  a  village  chief.
14:409:34931:22:22:70:541:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Radcliffe-Brown  (1950,  p.42)  describes  this  form  of  organization,  referring  specifically  to  the
14:410:35037:22:44:70:541:480:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Lozi  and  Bemba  of  modern  Zambia:   “The  typical  corporate  group  in  that  region  is  a  village
14:411:35250:44:21:70:541:436:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a closed group;  that is, individuals or families may join or leave it, moving from one village to
14:412:35348:21:22:70:541:415:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:another.  It is usual that a number of the inhabitants of a village at any time should be related,
14:413:35446:22:22:70:541:393:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:either by cognatic ties or through marriage with the headman or with one another, but they do
14:414:35539:22:22:70:445:371:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not form a unilineal kin group, which is by its constitution a ‘closed’ group.”
14:415:35618:22:22:85:541:349:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Radcliffe-Brown (1950, p.43) also describes why unilineal descent (lineage traced through the
14:416:35711:22:22:70:541:327:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:male line only or the female line only) is important for segmentary lineage organization and why
14:417:35807:22:22:70:541:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cognatic descent (tracing lineage through both the male or female lines) is not compatible with
14:418:35902:22:22:70:541:283:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage organization:  “It is the corporate kin group. . . that controls the use of land,
14:419:36002:22:22:70:541:261:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whether  for  hunting,  for  pastoral  life,  or  for  cultivation;  that  exacts  vengeance  for  the  killing
14:420:36113:22:22:70:541:239:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  a  member,  or  demands  and  receives  an  indemnity. . . A  continuing  social  structure  requires
14:421:36218:22:22:70:541:217:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the aggregation of individuals into distinct separated groups, each with its own solidarity, every
14:422:36316:22:22:70:541:195:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:person belonging to one group of any set. . . In kinship systems cognatic kinship cannot provide
14:423:36412:22:22:70:541:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:this;  it  is  only  made  possible  by  the  use  of  the  principle  of  unilineal  descent.”7Analyses  of
14:424:36520:22:21:70:541:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cognatic kinship groups illustrate that they are very different in structure from segmentary lineage
14:425:36620:21:22:70:541:130:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups.  Most important for thinking about the mechanisms linking social structure and conflict
14:426:36715:22:20:70:541:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is  the  fact  that  segmentary  lineage  societies  are  closed  in  a  way  cognatic  societies  are  not  and
14:427:36827:20:14:83:541:88:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:7As  we  discuss  further  below,  one  of  the  primary  characteristics  of  segmentary  lineage  organizations,  which  is
14:428:36952:14:0:70:428:74:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:relevant for creating an ethnicity-level measure is whether a society has unilineal descent.
15:429:37046:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  all  of  the  functions  that  a  corporate  group  might  undertake  –  social,  political,  judicial,  or
15:430:37159:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:administrative – are fused together in a segmentary lineage group. These elements seem to create
15:431:37255:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a far greater social solidarity in segmentary lineage societies and much greater ability to engage in
15:432:37356:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:collective action.  This is not so in societies with cognatic kinship, where there is typically a clear
15:433:37459:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:differentiation  between  kinship  relations  and  political  relations  (Fortes,1953,  p.26;  Gluckman,
15:434:37563:22:22:70:127:614:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:1951, p.31).
15:435:37575:22:22:85:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Writing about the Lozi of Zambia, Max Gluckman (1950) makes a similar point: “No corporate
15:436:37665:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:unilineal group of kinsmen exists among the Lozi.  Every child. . . has a right to make its home in
15:437:37764:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a village of either of its mother’s parents and to inherit there.  It also has these rights with the
15:438:37864:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:kin of its father. . . There are no broadly based unilineal groups associating in common rights of
15:439:37962:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:residence,  ownership,  inheritance,  production  etc.”  (Gluckman,1950,  pp.171,173).   Thus,  it  is
15:440:38064:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:clear that the social organization of ethnic groups, like the Bemba or Lozi, who base groups on
15:441:38159:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:villages,  is  very  different  from  segmentary  lineage  organization,  in  which  kinship  ties  are  pre-
15:442:38268:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:determined,  clearly defined,  and form distinct non-overlapping groups (e.g.,  segments).  While
15:443:38365:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the Bemba and Lozi had centralized states, their form of village/chief organization can also be
15:444:38460:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:found among ethnic groups that were stateless,  such as  the nearby Tonga  (Colson,1951).  This
15:445:38555:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:system is also common among groups in other parts of Africa, with the most well-studied groups
15:446:38649:22:22:70:522:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:being the Wabena of Tanzania and the Ankole and Toro of Uganda (Gluckman,1950, p.178).
15:447:38735:22:22:85:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In addition to cognatic kinship societies, there are a number of other forms of non-segmentary
15:448:38829:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  organization.   For  example,  there  are  societies,  like  the  Masai  in  Kenya  and  Tanzania,
15:449:38936:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whose politics and administration are organized by age – i.e., around age-sets – and by lineage or
15:450:39034:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:descent.  Age-based organization also create obligations although to those within one’s own age
15:451:39129:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:set. One could also imagine that age could also provide a useful axis for mobilization and collec-
15:452:39227:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tive action and there is some evidence that it certain instances it can, either historically (Gluckman,
15:453:39330:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:1940, Eldredge,2014) or in the modern period (Kurimoto and Simonse,1998).  However, what is
15:454:39421:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:distinct  about  segmentary  lineage  societies  is  the  number  of  individuals  that  can  be  mobilized
15:455:39528:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:through lineage relative to age sets. While an age grade typically consists of tens of people lineage
15:456:39629:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segments consist of hundreds or even thousands of people.  Another example is very small scale
15:457:39723:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:societies  that  never  develop  either  unilineal  or  cognatic  kinship  in  any  institutionalized  form.
15:458:39831:22:0:70:377:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Examples include such groups as the Hadza or the San people.
16:459:39893:0:34:70:111:724:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.  Data
16:460:39901:34:29:70:202:690:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:A.  Conflict Data (ACLED)
16:461:39926:29:22:70:541:661:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Our conflict data are from theArmed Conflict Location and Event Data Project(ACLED) database,
16:462:40019:22:22:70:541:639:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:which  provides  details  of  all  known  conflict  events  within  Africa  from  January1,1997to  De-
16:463:40121:22:22:70:541:617:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cember31,2014.  The information available includes the location (latitude and longitude) of the
16:464:40216:22:22:70:541:595:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict incident, the type of incident (riots and protests, battles, violence against civilians, etc),
16:465:40319:22:22:70:541:573:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  actors  involved  (government  forces,  rebel  militia,  civilians,  protestors,  etc),  the  motivation
16:466:40428:22:22:70:541:551:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  the  actors  involve  (e.g.,  aimed  at  taking  over  land,  riots,  protests,  etc),  and  the  number  of
16:467:40540:22:22:70:541:529:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fatalities during the event.  ACLED only includes conflict incidents in the data set if the province
16:468:40640:22:22:70:541:507:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in which the incident took place is known. Conflicts in which only the province, and not a smaller
16:469:40738:22:22:70:541:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:administrative unit,  is known are coded as having low geographic precision and are often,  but
16:470:40833:22:22:70:541:463:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not always, assigned the location of the province capital.  These conflicts make up4.75% of the
16:471:40928:22:22:70:159:441:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:full ACLED data.8
16:472:40945:22:22:85:541:419:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Given the potentially different effects that segmentary lineage structures have on civil conflicts
16:473:41043:22:21:70:541:397:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relative  to  other  forms  of  conflict,  such  as  within-ethnicity  conflicts,  our  analysis  examines  the
16:474:41154:21:22:70:541:376:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:following measures of conflict:  (1) an aggregate measure that includes all conflict incidents;  (2)
16:475:41254:22:22:70:541:354:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:incidents that are part of a civil war; (3) incidents that are part of a conflict that is not a civil war;
16:476:41360:22:22:70:540:332:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(4) incidents that are between individuals from the same ethnic group or village.  We provide a
16:477:41455:22:34:70:226:310:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:precise definition of each below.
16:478:41488:34:22:84:541:276:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:A:1.All  Conflicts.Includes  all  conflict  incidents  listed  in  the  ACLED  database  (with  the
16:479:41585:22:31:98:331:254:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:exclusion of conflicts that result in no fatalities).
16:480:41638:31:22:84:541:223:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:A:2.Civil  Conflict.Includes  conflict  incidents  that  involve  the  government  military  or  rebels
16:481:41739:22:31:98:454:201:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:A:(who are seeking to replace the central government) as one of the actors.9
16:482:41813:31:22:84:541:170:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:A:3.Non-Civil Conflict.Includes all conflict incidents that are not coded as being part of a civil
16:483:41909:22:16:98:144:148:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:A:conflict.10
16:484:41920:16:13:83:501:132:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:8All baseline results excluding conflicts with low geographic precision are reported in Tables A5and A8.
16:485:42024:13:13:83:529:119:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:9In the ACLED database, this includes all incidents for which the interaction variable is any integer from10–28.
16:486:42136:13:0:79:529:106:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:10In the ACLED database, this includes all incidents for which the interaction variable is any integer from30–67.
17:487:42251:0:22:84:541:724:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:A:4.Within-Group Conflict.Includes conflict incidents for which both actors in the conflict are
17:488:42344:22:34:98:358:702:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:A:geographically local and/or ethnically local groups.11
17:489:42398:34:22:85:541:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:For  each  of  the  four  types  of  conflict,  we  construct  three  measures  of  the  frequency  and
17:490:42501:22:22:70:541:646:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:prevalence  of  each  type:   the  number  of  deadly  conflict  incidents,  number  of  conflict  deaths,
17:491:42607:22:22:70:541:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and number of months from1997–2014with a deadly conflict incident.12In total, we have twelve
17:492:42699:22:22:70:214:602:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:different measures of conflict.
17:493:42732:22:43:85:541:580:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Following the methodology of previous studies (e.g., Michalopoulos and Papaioannou,2016),
17:494:42930:43:22:70:541:537:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:location of the conflict event with a digitized version of the map of ethnic boundaries taken from
17:495:43028:22:22:70:541:515:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Murdock (1959) to construct measures of the frequency and intensity of conflicts occurring within
17:496:43125:22:22:70:541:493:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the territory of each ethnic group.14The use of location to infer those who are involved in the
17:497:43220:22:22:70:541:471:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflicts is motivated by the fact that, in general, conflicts tend to occur close to the homelands
17:498:43319:22:22:70:541:449:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  participants.    This  is  most  clearly  true  for  disputes  and  conflicts  that  do  not  involve  the
17:499:43429:22:22:70:541:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:government military, which tend to be very localized.  For conflicts that involve the government
17:500:43525:22:22:70:541:405:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:military – i.e., conflicts that we refer to as civil conflicts – conflicts also generally occur within the
17:501:43631:22:22:70:541:383:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ethnic homelands of the combatants.  (See for example the recent findings of Michalopoulos and
17:502:43725:22:22:70:541:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Papaioannou (2016).)  Therefore, for these forms of conflicts as well, within which ethnic group’s
17:503:43823:22:22:70:278:339:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:territory the fighting occurs is informative.
17:504:43868:22:22:85:541:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:A shortcoming of our strategy is that conflicts that involve members of an ethnic group but
17:505:43959:22:22:70:541:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:occur outside of the group’ boundaries will not be correctly identified in our estimates. Although
17:506:44057:22:21:70:541:273:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:it  would  also  be  informative  to  connect  ethnic  groups  to  conflict  by  using  information  on  the
17:507:44165:21:22:70:541:252:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:participants involved, unfortunately this strategy is not feasible.  It requires detailed information
17:508:44266:22:22:70:541:230:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on the ethnicity of the parties involved in each conflict,  which is not available.  Often,  we only
17:509:44366:22:20:70:541:208:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:have a very general description of the participants, such as “locals”, “protestors”, “civilians”, etc.
17:510:44468:20:14:79:541:188:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:11This includes values of the interaction variable from40–47,50–57and60–67. We exclude conflicts in which one of
17:511:44580:14:10:70:398:174:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:the participants is listed as “other," defined as “outside/external force (e.g., UN).”
17:512:44666:10:12:79:402:164:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:12By ‘deadly’ conflicts we mean a conflict that results in at least one battle death.
17:513:44751:12:15:79:541:152:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:13All  are  positively  correlated  and  the  correlation  coefficients  range  from0.489–0.837.   The  lowest  correlation  is
17:514:44878:15:9:70:541:137:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:between civil conflicts and within-group conflicts and the highest correlation is between all conflicts and civil conflicts.
17:515:45002:9:14:79:541:128:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:14The digitized map is taken from Nunn (2008) and is the same map as used in Michalopoulos and Papaioannou
17:516:45108:14:0:70:142:114:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:(2013,2014,2016).
18:517:45127:0:30:70:287:724:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:B.  Identifying Segmentary Lineage Societies
18:518:45171:30:22:70:541:694:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The most commonly used source for ethnographic information is theEthnographic Atlas,  which
18:519:45262:22:22:70:541:672:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:contains information on the traditional practices and characteristics of1,265ethnic groups.  Al-
18:520:45358:22:22:70:541:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:though this source does include a number of characteristics of kinship practices, it does not con-
18:521:45456:22:21:70:541:628:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tain information on whether a society is organized according to segmentary lineages.15Therefore,
18:522:45552:21:22:70:541:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:to identify the presence or absence of a segmentary lineage system, we relied on theEthnographic
18:523:45648:22:22:70:541:585:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:Survey  of  Africa,  which  is  a  multi-volume  work  that  compiles  ethnographic  information  from
18:524:45750:22:22:70:541:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a  large  number  of  African  ethnic  groups.   TheSurvey,  edited  by  Daryll  Forde,  was  published
18:525:45853:22:22:70:541:541:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:over the course of several decades, beginning during the late-1940s, by the International African
18:526:45950:22:22:70:541:519:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Institute  in  London.   It  is  divided  into  individual  volumes,  first  by  region  and  then  by  ethnic
18:527:46060:22:22:70:541:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:group,  and  each  entry  contains  detailed  information  about  the  political,  social,  cultural,  and
18:528:46166:22:22:70:541:475:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:economic practices of each ethnic group, as well as a description of the ecological environment
18:529:46261:22:22:70:541:453:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:inhabited  by  the  group.   If  a  particular  group  was  not  included  in  theEthnographic  Survey  of
18:530:46367:22:22:70:541:431:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:Africa, or when the information available was insufficient to determine whether or not it was a
18:531:46462:22:22:70:541:409:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage society, we then consulted additional sources, including the references used
18:532:46557:22:22:70:540:387:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:in theEthnographic Atlasto try to determine if the group had a segmentary lineage structure.16
18:533:46651:22:22:70:464:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Full details of the data construction are provided in the paper’s online appendix.
18:534:46733:22:21:85:541:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:For a group to be coded as a segmentary lineage society, we required that it satisfy the follow-
18:535:46829:21:22:70:541:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ing three criteria,  which are taken from Middleton and Tait’s (1958) definition of a segmentary
18:536:46925:22:31:70:143:300:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage society.
18:537:46941:31:22:84:540:269:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:A:1.  The  society  must  be  based  on  unilineal  descent  and  there  must  have  been  direct  and
18:538:47041:22:22:98:541:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:explicit evidence that people identify with their lineages and are aware of their genealogical
18:539:47135:22:31:98:318:225:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:connections to members of other sub-groups.
18:540:47178:31:22:84:540:194:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:A:2.  The segments of the lineages must take on a ‘corporate form’, which means that branching
18:541:47270:22:19:98:541:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:lineage segments must determine administrative functions and political allegiances and that
18:542:47361:19:14:79:541:153:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:15TheEthnographic Atlashas information on the presence of clans and whether living arrangements are organized
18:543:47470:14:11:70:541:139:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:around them (variables v15/v16) and whether there are lineages that are unilineal (matrilineal or patrilineal) (v17/v19).
18:544:47591:11:11:70:541:128:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:However, whether or not a society had a segmentary lineage structure is not a simple composition of these. Although
18:545:47706:11:11:70:541:117:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:these measures are correlated with our constructed segmentary lineage variable, the two variables only explain about
18:546:47822:11:10:70:264:106:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:11% of the total variation in segmentary lineage.
18:547:47871:10:14:79:541:96:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:16In total, for111of the145ethnic groups coded, information was from theEthnographic Survey of Africa.  For the
18:548:47982:14:11:70:541:82:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:remaining  groups,  information  was  taken  from  a  number  of  other  sources,  which  are  documented  in  the  paper’s
18:549:48105:11:0:70:110:71:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:appendix.
19:550:48116:0:31:98:540:724:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:A:a centralized political authority entirely divorced from the lineage structure does not exist.17
19:551:48212:31:22:84:540:693:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:A:3.  Lineage and genealogical relationships affect where people live, with those who are more
19:552:48304:22:22:98:541:671:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:closely related living geographically closer to one another.  Thus, we require evidence that
19:553:48396:22:31:98:508:649:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:A:there is a geographic organization of residence that is based on the lineage system.18
19:554:48482:31:22:85:541:618:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:For an ethnic group to be coded as a segmentary lineage society, we required direct evidence
19:555:48574:22:22:70:541:596:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  each  of  the  three  criteria  is  satisfied.Likewise,  for  an  ethnic  group  to  be  coded  as  a
19:556:48681:22:22:70:541:574:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:non-segmentary lineage society, we required direct evidence that any of the three criteria is not
19:557:48778:22:21:70:541:552:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:satisfied.  That is, lack of evidence for a criterion was not sufficient for a variable to be coded as
19:558:48880:21:22:70:541:531:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not being a segmentary lineage system.  In the end, we are able to code our segmentary lineage
19:559:48974:22:22:70:541:509:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:society  indicator  variable  for145ethnic  groups  within  Africa  (using  the  ethnicity  classification
19:560:49080:22:22:70:541:487:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  Murdock  (1959)).   For  the  other  ethnic  groups,  the  existing  evidence  was  not  sufficient  to
19:561:49187:22:22:70:541:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:determine with confidence whether an ethnic group is based on segmentary lineage organization
19:562:49280:22:22:70:540:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:or not.  Although we do not have data for all ethnic groups in sub-Saharan Africa, the145ethnic
19:563:49375:22:22:70:393:421:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:groups account for38% of the population of sub-Saharan Africa.19
19:564:49439:22:22:85:541:399:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:As a check on the validity of our coding, after the variable was constructed, we consulted the
19:565:49533:22:22:70:541:377:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:existing secondary literature for cases where scholars had previously characterized or described
19:566:49629:22:22:70:541:355:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:specific ethnic groups as having a segmentary lineage organization or not.  Reassuringly,  in all
19:567:49726:22:22:70:541:333:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cases (42in total), our classification matched the majority consensus. These cases are summarized
19:568:49823:22:22:70:197:311:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:in the paper’s appendix.20
19:569:49849:22:22:85:541:289:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The145ethnic  groups  are  shown  in  Figures2a  and2b.   Segmentary  lineage  societies  are
19:570:49942:22:21:70:541:267:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:depicted in dark grey and non-segmentary lineage societies in light grety.  The map shows that
19:571:50036:21:22:70:541:246:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our sample includes ethnic groups from many parts of Africa. In Figure2b, we add the locations
19:572:50130:22:22:70:541:224:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of conflict incidents in the ACLED dataset that occur within the boundaries of the ethnic groups
19:573:50226:22:20:70:140:202:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in our sample.
19:574:50240:20:13:79:541:182:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:17On the importance of this aspect of segmentary lineage organization, see Evans-Pritchard and Fortes (1940, p.13).
19:575:50355:13:14:79:541:169:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:18On  the  importance  of  this  aspect  of  segmentary  lineage  organization,  see  Radcliffe-Brown  (1950,  p.42),  Fortes
19:576:50480:14:9:70:220:155:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:(1953, p.36), or Sahlins (1961, p.328).
19:577:50519:9:15:79:541:146:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:19The figures are calculated using NASAEarthDataestimates of population density in2000and Murdock’s ethnic
19:578:50625:15:9:70:149:131:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:boundary shapefile.
19:579:50644:9:14:79:541:122:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:20This is not to say that there is always unanimity within the literature about the classification of every society.  For
19:580:50765:14:11:70:541:108:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:example, Sahlins (1961) argues that the Dinka are not a segmentary lineage society, while Butt (1952) and Middleton
19:581:50880:11:11:70:541:97:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:and  Tait  (1958)  argue  that  they  are.   The  difference  arises  because  Sahlins  appears  to  have  been  using  a  narrower
19:582:51011:11:0:70:269:86:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:definition of segmentary lineage than is standard.
20:583:51063:0:288:233:378:415:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:(a) Segmentary lineage classification
20:584:51100:288:23:189:423:127:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:(b) Segmentary lineage classification and conflict incidents
20:585:51160:23:13:70:541:104:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure2:  Maps showing the boundaries of ethnic groups, the presence and absence of segmentary
20:586:51254:13:14:70:540:91:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  organization,  and,  in  Figure2b,  the  location  of  conflict  incidents  that  occur  within  the
20:587:51363:14:0:70:299:77:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:boundaries of the ethnic groups in our sample.
21:588:51411:0:22:85:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:To better understand the extent to which our sample of145ethnic groups is representative of
21:589:51502:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the full population of societies within sub-Saharan Africa, we compare the characteristics of the
21:590:51599:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ethnic groups within our sample to the ethnic groups outside of our sample. This can be done for
21:591:51695:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:any of the variables that are available from theEthnographic Atlasor for geographic characteristics.
21:592:51795:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:Within theEthnographic Atlas, there are420ethnic groups from sub-Saharan Africa. Of these,145
21:593:51888:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are in our sample and275are not.  In Table1, we report averages of both groups for a number
21:594:51979:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of characteristics, as well as their differences in means and statistical significance.  We find that
21:595:52080:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for16of the19variables examined, there is no statistically significant difference between the two
21:596:52177:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups (at the5% level or stronger).  The three measures for which the samples appear different
21:597:52272:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are:   jurisdictional  hierarchy,  the  natural  log  of  total  population,  and  longitude.   Thus,  larger
21:598:52381:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups that have a more centralized political system are more likely to be in our sample.  This is
21:599:52479:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:explained by the fact that larger ethnic groups were more likely to be studied and documented
21:600:52572:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by anthropologists and therefore are more likely to appear in our sample. This difference should
21:601:52668:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be kept in mind when interpreting our results.  The explanation for the difference in longitude is
21:602:52766:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:less clear. Our sample is slightly more likely to include ethnic groups from the eastern portion of
21:603:52865:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Africa.  It is possible that ethnic groups in the region were studied in greater detail than ethnic
21:604:52964:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups in other regions.  It is also possible that it is simply due to the large number of variables
21:605:53064:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that we examine.  With almost20variables being examined, it is expected that even with balance
21:606:53158:22:38:70:476:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:one of the twenty will be significantly different from zero at a5% significance level.
21:607:53244:38:30:70:192:291:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:C.  Descriptive Statistics
21:608:53270:30:22:70:541:261:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:Within  the  sample  of145ethnic  groups,74have  a  segmentary  lineage  organization,  while71
21:609:53365:22:22:70:541:239:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:do not.  Average characteristics of the two groups, as well as the differences between them, are
