21:612:53647:22:22:70:541:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:column3reports the difference in means between the two groups, as well as the standard error
21:613:53739:22:21:70:152:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the difference.

24:728:60558:22:22:85:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In all cases but one,  the difference between the two groups is not statistically different from
24:729:60654:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:zero.    Particularly  noteworthy  is  the  similarity  between  the  two  groups  in  terms  of  reliance
24:730:60760:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on  animal  husbandry.   This  alleviates  concerns  that  segmentary  lineage  organization  might  be
24:731:60863:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:correlated with the practice of animal husbandry, which has been hypothesized to be associated
24:732:60957:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with a ‘culture of honor’, which can lead to the escalation of violence and conflict (Nisbett and
24:733:61054:22:22:70:212:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Cohen,1996, Grosjean,2014).
24:734:61081:22:21:85:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The one measure that is statistically different between the two groups is the number of levels of
24:735:61178:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:jurisdictional hierarchy beyond the local community. This is a particularly important characteris-
24:736:61276:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tic, especially given the existing evidence that this is associated with better development outcomes
24:737:61376:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:today (Gennaioli and Rainer,2007, Michalopoulos and Papaioannou,2013).  It is plausible that
24:738:61468:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups with a history of statelessness might experience more conflicts today.  However, it is also
24:739:61566:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:worth noting that although segmentary lineage societies tend to be less centralized on average, the
24:740:61665:22:22:70:540:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:difference of0.34between the two groups is small.  This reflects the fact that many segmentary
24:741:61759:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  societies  had  experienced  processes  of  political  centralization.   Indeed,  Southall  (1956)
24:742:61866:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:pioneered  the  term  ‘segmentary  state’  to  refer  to  the  co-existence  of  these  different  structures.
24:743:61976:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Thus, lineage organization was compatible both with large centralized states and with societies
24:744:62071:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  were  stateless.   To  illustrate  this,  in  Figure3we  categorize  our  societies  into  four  groups
24:745:62180:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:depending on: (1) whether or not they have a segmentary lineage structure, and (2) whether or not
24:746:62277:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:they are politically centralized (defined as having two or more levels of political authority beyond
24:747:62377:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  local  community).   To  define  centralized  and  stateless  societies,  we  use  information  on  the
24:748:62485:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:levels of political authority beyond the local community from variablev33from theEthnographic
24:749:62578:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:Atlas. Stateless societies are defined as having0or1levels, while centralized societies are defined
24:750:62677:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as  having2–4levels.   As  shown,  there  are  examples  of  ethnic  groups  in  all  four  groups,  and
24:751:62781:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:they are distributed fairly equally between the different cells.  This is consistence with the small
24:752:62881:22:22:70:204:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:difference found in Table2.
24:753:62908:22:22:85:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Given  the  difference  in  state  centralization  observed  between  the  societies  with  segmentary
24:754:63010:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineages  and  those  without  and  the  importance  of  state  centralization  for  long-run  economic
24:755:63113:22:22:70:541:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:development (and potentially conflict), in all specifications, we control for historical state central-

25:765:63653:47:33:70:165:538:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:C:4.  OLS Estimates
25:766:63670:33:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We now turn to OLS estimates of the relationship between segmentary lineage organization and
25:767:63762:22:33:70:388:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict today. For this, we use the following estimating equation:

25:770:63945:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f19:B:experienced  by  ethnic  groupi.ISLiis  an  indicator  variable  that  equals  one  if  ethnic  groupi
25:771:64047:22:22:70:540:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:has  a  segmentary  lineage  organization  and  zero  if  it  does  not.αc(i)denotes  country  fixed
25:772:64147:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:effects.X′iis  a  vector  of  ethnicity-level  historical  and  geographic  covariates.   The  geographic
25:773:64252:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:controls are:  the natural log of the land area occupied by the ethnic group, the natural log of the
25:774:64352:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:minimum distance between the ethnic group centroid and a national border, an indicator variable
25:775:64447:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  equals  one  if  the  ethnic  group  is  cut  by  a  national  border,  average  altitude,  the  absolute
25:776:64558:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:value  of  latitude,  longitude,  and  average  agricultural  suitability.    The  historical  controls  are:
25:777:64667:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:pre-industrial  political  centralization  (levels  of  political  authority  beyond  the  local  community)
25:778:64775:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  pre-industrial  economic  development  measured  by  the  complexity  of  settlement  patterns,
25:779:64875:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:which is measured on a1–8integer scale.22The coefficient of interest isβ.  A positive coefficient
25:780:64972:22:22:70:401:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:indicates that segmentary lineage societies experience more conflict.
25:781:65041:22:22:85:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Estimates of equation (1) are reported in Table3.  Each panel reports estimates for one of the
25:782:65135:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:four conflict types: all conflicts, civil conflicts, non-civil conflicts, and within-group conflicts. Each
25:783:65241:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:triplet of columns reports estimates for one of our three measures of conflict intensity: the natural
25:784:65342:22:19:70:541:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:log of the total number of dearly conflict incidents (columns1–3), the natural log of the number
25:785:65438:19:0:79:520:69:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:22The finer details of the construction and measurement of the covariates is provided in the paper’s appendix.
26:786:65550:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  conflict  deaths  (column4–6),  or  the  natural  log  of  the  number  of  months  of  deadly  conflict
26:787:65658:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(columns7–9).  For each outcome variable,  we report three specifications,  each with a different
26:788:65755:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:set  of  covariates.  The  first  specification  (in  columns1,4,  and7)  is  the  most  parsimonious  and
26:789:65861:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:only includes country fixed effects. The second specification (in columns2,5, and8) also controls
26:790:65958:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for the geographic covariates.  The final specification (in columns3,6,  and9) also includes the
26:791:66054:22:22:70:169:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:historical covariates.
26:792:66076:22:22:85:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Across  all36specifications,  we  estimate  a  positive  and  significant  relationship  between  the
26:793:66177:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:presence of segmentary lineage organization and conflict. In addition to being statistically signif-
26:794:66277:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:icant, the estimates are also quantitatively meaningful.  For example, according to the estimates
26:795:66374:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for the number of deadly conflict incidents (columns1–3of panel A), a segmentary lineage society
26:796:66470:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:experiences80–110%  more  incidents  than  a  society  that  does  not  have  a  segmentary  lineage
26:797:66570:22:22:70:532:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization. The magnitudes of the effects are fairly similar across the different conflict types.
26:798:66669:22:22:85:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In  Figures4a–4d,  we  report  partial  correlation  plots  for  each  type  of  conflict,  measured  by
26:799:66773:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:number of incidents, and from the specification that includes country fixed effects, the geographic
26:800:66872:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:controls, and the historical controls (column3).  For each conflict type, the relationship appears
26:801:66970:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:general and to not be driven by a small number of influential observations.  Interestingly, the fit
26:802:67069:22:22:70:325:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:appears tightest for localized within-group conflicts.
26:803:67123:22:22:85:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In the figures,  we label each observation with the name of the ethnicity.  This allows one to
26:804:67217:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:identify the location of ethnic groups that have been widely studied in the anthropology literature.
26:805:67317:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:One  example  of  such  a  group  is  the  Lele,  who  are  from  the  Kasai  province  of  the  Democratic
26:806:67424:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Republic of the Congo.  They are a society that is not based on segmentary lineage, but instead
26:807:67519:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on age sets (Douglas,1963).  Further, this has been an area of the country with little large-scale
26:808:67617:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict.  The Lele appear in the bottom left of the figures.  Also noteworthy are the Bemba and
26:809:67713:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Toro, two societies identified by anthropologists as not having segmentary lineage structures and
26:810:67810:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:experiencing relatively little conflict.  The Bemba are behind the left side of the trend line,  and
26:811:67910:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  Toro  are  just  above  the  left  side  of  the  trend  line,  seen  most  clearly  in  Figure4a  and4b.
26:812:68020:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:By  contrast,  in  the  upper  right  of  the  figure  are  such  societies  as  the  Kissi,  in  Sierra  Leone,  a
26:813:68135:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage society whose territory experienced a great deal of conflict during the Sierra
26:814:68232:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Leone civil war (Middleton and Tait,1958, Massing,1980). We also see the Songhai, a segmentary
26:815:68326:22:22:70:541:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage group from Mali and Niger (Rouch,1954), as well as the Douala, a segmentary lineage
26:816:68417:22:0:70:332:66:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:group from Cameroon (Ardener,1956, Terretta,2013).

28:1238:75516:35:29:70:272:264:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:A.  Assessing Selection on Unobservables
28:1239:75556:29:22:70:541:235:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:While the RD analysis that we undertake below is our primary strategy for estimating the causal
28:1240:75651:22:22:70:541:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relationship between segmentary lineage organization and conflict, in this section we undertake
28:1241:75746:22:22:70:438:191:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a number of additional exercises to assess the validity of the OLS estimates.
28:1242:75823:22:22:85:541:169:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We  start  by  first  assessing  the  sensitivity  of  the  OLS  estimates  to  controlling  for  observable
28:1243:75931:22:22:70:541:147:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:characteristics.   We  first  employ  the  strategy  adapted  by  Nunn  and  Wantchekon  (2011)  from
28:1244:76032:22:22:70:541:125:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Altonji,  Elder  and  Taber  (2005)  that  allows  us  to  determine  how  much  stronger  selection  on
28:1245:76136:22:22:70:541:103:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:unobservables would have to be compared to selection on observables in order to fully explain
28:1246:76229:22:22:70:541:81:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:away  our  results.   To  perform  this  test,  we  calculate  the  ratioˆβF/(ˆβR−ˆβF),  whereˆβFis  our
28:1247:76333:22:0:70:541:59:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:coefficient  of  interest  from  a  regression  that  includes  a  full  set  of  controls  whileˆβRis  our
29:1248:76442:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:coefficient  of  interest  from  a  regression  that  includes  a  restricted  set  of  controls.   The  results
29:1249:76554:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are  reported  in  columns1–3of  Appendix  Table  A2.Each  panel  reports  a  ratio  where  the
29:1250:76649:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fully-controlled  regression  includes  the  geographic  and  historical  controls,  while  the  restricted
29:1251:76756:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:regression including country fixed effects only. This yields twelve ratios that range from−160.24
29:1252:76853:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to 193.71.  In some cases,  the coefficient in the fully-controlled model is larger than that on the
29:1253:76953:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:uncontrolled  model  giving  a  negative  ratio.   In  general,  these  ratios  suggest  that  the  influence
29:1254:77062:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  unobservable  characteristics  would  have  to  be  far  greater  than  the  influence  of  observable
29:1255:77168:22:22:70:300:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:characteristics to fully account for our findings.
29:1256:77218:22:21:85:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We  also  use  the  method  from  Oster  (2017)  to  calculate  a  lower  bound  for  our  coefficient  of
29:1257:77324:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:interest.   Oster  shows  that  if  one  assumes  that  observables  and  unobservables  have  the  same
29:1258:77428:22:20:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f21:B:explanatory  power  in  the  outcome  variable,  then  the  following  is  a  consistent  estimator:β∗=
29:1259:77531:20:7:75:199:485:11:g_d0_f4:6:g_d0_f28:A:ˆβF−(ˆβR−ˆβF)×R2max−R2F
29:1260:77554:7:0:164:237:478:8:g_d0_f20:11:g_d0_f4:A:R2F−R2R, where
29:1261:77568:0:24:245:541:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:ˆβFandˆβRare as defined above,R2Fis theR-squared from the
29:1262:77625:24:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fully-controlled regression, andR2Ris theR-squared from the restricted regression.R2is the
29:1263:77718:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f4:B:R-squared from a regression that includes all observable and unobservable controls. Although in
29:1264:77813:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:theory, the maximum possible value ofR2maxis one, as Gonzalez and Miguel (2015) have shown,
29:1265:77904:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  the  real  world,  where  there  is  significant  measurement  error,  the  value  ofR2maxshould  be
29:1266:78008:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:much  lower  than  one.   However,  in  order  to  produce  the  most  conservative  estimates,  we  set
29:1267:78112:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f4:B:R2max=1.  The lower bound estimates are reported in columns4–6of Appendix Table A2.  All
29:1268:78200:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lower bound estimates from this exercise remain positive and, taken at face value, still imply a
29:1269:78296:22:22:70:419:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sizeable estimated effect of segmentary lineage organization on conflict.
29:1270:78369:22:22:85:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:An alternative strategy to OLS is to use matching to compare each segmentary lineage society
29:1271:78461:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to  the  non-segmentary  lineage  society  that  is  most  similar,  based  on  a  range  of  observable
29:1272:78565:21:22:70:540:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:characteristics.23We report such matching estimates in Appendix Table A3.  Column1reports
29:1273:78654:22:22:70:540:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates where ethnicity pairs are matched on latitude and longitude only.  Column2reports
29:1274:78745:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates  from  matching  based  on  the  baseline  set  of  geographic  and  historical  controls  from
29:1275:78850:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:equation (1).  Column3reports estimates from matching the geographic and historical controls,
29:1276:78943:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:but  where  we  also  require  that  members  of  a  matched  pair  have  the  same  number  of  levels  of
29:1277:79050:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:jurisdictional  hierarchy  beyond  the  local  community.   This  is  motivated  by  the  importance  of
29:1278:79154:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:accounting  for  political  centralization  as  thoroughly  as  possible.   As  reported,  for  each  conflict
29:1279:79264:22:19:70:407:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:outcome, the estimates continue to be positive and highly significant.
29:1280:79334:19:0:79:355:69:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:23We use nearest neighbor matching based on Mahalanobis distance.
30:1281:79401:0:30:70:179:724:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:B.  Robustness Checks
30:1282:79422:30:22:70:541:694:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  now  turn  to  an  examination  of  the  robustness  and  sensitivity  of  the  OLS  estimates.   Given
30:1283:79529:22:22:70:541:672:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  all  of  our  conflict  measures  are  count  variables,  we  check  that  our  estimates  are  robust  to
30:1284:79641:22:22:70:541:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:using a Poisson or negative binomial estimator. Table A4reports estimates for the most stringent
30:1285:79737:22:21:70:541:628:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:specification that includes country fixed effects, geographic controls, and the historical controls.
30:1286:79837:21:22:70:541:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Our  findings  remain  robust.In  every  specification,  the  estimated  relationship  between  the
30:1287:79936:22:22:70:541:585:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage and conflict is positive, sizeable, and in all specifications but one, statistically
30:1288:80039:22:22:70:123:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:significant.
30:1289:80051:22:22:85:541:541:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We  next  check  the  robustness  of  our  estimates  to  alternative  measures  of  conflict.One
30:1290:80148:22:22:70:541:519:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:characteristic  of  the  ACLED  conflict  data  is  that  they  include  a  wide  range  of  different  activi-
30:1291:80259:22:22:70:541:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ties  as  incidents,  sometimes  activities  of  conflict  actors  that  are  part  of  larger  conflicts  but  are
30:1292:80374:22:22:70:541:475:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not  themselves  explicitly  violent.   These  include  (i)  instances  when  a  headquarters  or  base  is
30:1293:80481:22:22:70:541:453:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:established, (ii) non-violent activity by a conflict actor, and (iii) a non-violent transfer of territory.
30:1294:80587:22:22:70:541:431:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We construct versions of our outcome variables that exclude conflict events that are in the ACLED
30:1295:80684:22:22:70:541:409:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:database  but  are  “non-violent.”  While  our  baseline  conflict  measures  already  exclude  conflicts
30:1296:80789:22:22:70:541:387:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:without fatalities, excluding conflicts classified as non-violent on the basis of the actors’ intentions
30:1297:80893:22:22:70:541:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is another strategy to check that our conflict measures capture variation in violent conflict.  The
30:1298:80992:22:21:70:540:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates using this alternative measure are reported in panel A of Appendix Table A5.  We find
30:1299:81087:21:22:70:489:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that our estimates remain robust to using this alternative measure of conflict intensity.
30:1300:81176:22:22:85:541:300:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We also check the robustness of our estimates to the use of data from an alternative commonly-
30:1301:81270:22:22:70:541:278:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:used source of conflict data, theUppsala Conflict Data Program - Georeferenced Event Dataset(UCDP
30:1302:81367:22:22:70:541:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:GED). There are a number of differences between this data source and the ACLED source that
30:1303:81457:22:22:70:541:234:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we use.  First, this source begins in1991, six years earlier than the ACLED data.  Second, unlike
30:1304:81554:22:22:70:541:212:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the ACLED data, this source has a minimum mortality threshold (25fatalities in a calendar year)
30:1305:81649:22:22:70:541:190:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that  has  to  be  met  for  the  conflict  to  appear  in  the  dataset.   Thus,  checking  the  robustness  of
30:1306:81761:22:22:70:541:168:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our findings to this alternative data source also checks the robustness of our estimates to using
30:1307:81858:22:22:70:540:146:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:a  slightly  different  time  period  and  a  higher  death  threshold.   Panel  B  of  Appendix  Table  A5
30:1308:81965:22:22:70:541:124:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:reports the estimates using the UCDP GED conflict data.  The estimates remain very similar to
30:1309:82058:22:22:70:180:102:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our baseline estimates.
30:1310:82081:22:22:85:541:80:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Another potential concern is that our results may be driven by a small number of particularly
30:1311:82174:22:0:70:541:58:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:influential  outlying  observations.    One  is  particularly  concerned  that  observations  with  very
31:1312:82280:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:intensive fighting may have particularly strong leverage in the regressions.  An example would
31:1313:82374:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be  the  ethnic groups  that experienced the conflicts that  were initiated by the Lord’s Resistance
31:1314:82474:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Army in Uganda.  These conflicts primarily occurred within the territory of segmentary lineage
31:1315:82568:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:societies like the Acholi.  Although the partial correlation plots reported in Figures4a–4d seem
31:1316:82664:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to show that the estimates are fairly general and are not driven by a small number of influential
31:1317:82761:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:observations,  we  undertake  a  systematic  check  here.   Specifically,  we  re-estimate  our  baseline
31:1318:82866:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:specification after dropping influential observations that we identify using Cook’s Distance.  As
31:1319:82963:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an  alternative  strategy,  we  re-estimate  equation  (1),  after  removing  observations  with  extreme
31:1320:83068:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:values of conflict, defined as those within the top five percent. The estimates, which are reported
31:1321:83167:21:22:70:540:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in panels A and B of Appendix Table A6, show that both strategies yield estimates that are similar
31:1322:83265:22:22:70:191:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to the baseline estimates.
31:1323:83291:22:22:85:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  final  robustness  check  that  we  perform  includes  additional  covariates  in  our  estimating
31:1324:83394:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:equation.   In  our  baseline  specifications,  we  were  careful  not  to  include  variables  that  are  po-
31:1325:83504:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tentially endogenous to segmentary lineage organization.  However, with the standard concerns
31:1326:83597:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:associated with endogenous covariates in mind, we now check the sensitivity of our findings to
31:1327:83691:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:controlling for a number of potentially endogenous factors. The first that we consider is a society’s
31:1328:83792:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:history of conflict which, as Besley and Reynal-Querol (2014) document, is positively correlated
31:1329:83888:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with  the  prevalence  of  conflict  today.   Estimates  controlling  for  the  prevalence  of  pre-colonial
31:1330:83996:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflicts, using data from Besley and Reynal-Querol (2014), are reported in Appendix Table A7.
31:1331:84090:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Our results remain highly significant and the magnitude of the point estimates are very similar
31:1332:84185:22:22:70:200:285:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:to the baseline estimates.24
31:1333:84213:22:21:85:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We  next  check  the  sensitivity  of  our  estimates  to  controlling  for  ethnicity-level  measures  of
31:1334:84319:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:economic  prosperity  and  the  presence  of  Islam  today,  both  of  which  are  potentially  important
31:1335:84424:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:determinants  of  conflict.   We  include  two  measure  of  economic  prosperity:  the  natural  log  of
31:1336:84529:22:22:70:540:198:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:night  light  intensity  normalized  by  population,25and  the  natural  log  of  population  density.26
31:1337:84633:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To measure the presence of Islam, we use data from theWorld Religion Database, which records
31:1338:84725:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:religious affiliation for ethnicities in Africa, and construct an indicator variable that equals one if
31:1339:84828:22:19:70:345:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Islam is the dominant religion of the ethnic group today.
31:1340:84885:19:13:79:521:113:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:24The estimates in the table are directly comparable to the estimates reported in columns3,6, and9of Table3.
31:1341:84993:13:15:79:541:100:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:25The use of nightlights as a proxy for economic development follows, among others, Henderson, Storeygard and
31:1342:85102:15:9:70:461:85:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:Weil (2012), Michalopoulos and Papaioannou (2013), and Michalopoulos and Papaioannou (2014).
31:1343:85194:9:0:79:233:76:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:26Both variables are measured in2000.
32:1344:85233:0:22:85:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Estimates  of  equation  (1)  with  these  additional  covariates  are  reported  in  Appendix  Table
32:1345:85334:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:A8.  We find that even after accounting for these potentially endogenous factors,  the estimated
32:1346:85430:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relationship between segmentary lineage and conflict remains positive, although the magnitude
32:1347:85523:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the estimated effects decline slightly. Interestingly, the most notable decline is for civil conflicts,
32:1348:85629:22:40:70:453:636:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:while the decline is modest for non-civil conflicts and within-group conflicts.27
32:1349:85710:40:34:70:377:596:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:C:5.  Accounting for Unobservables: Spatial RD Estimates
32:1350:85764:34:22:70:541:562:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Despite  the  robustness  of  our  OLS  estimates  and  the  fact  that  our  findings  are  similar  when
32:1351:85870:22:22:70:541:540:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we  account  for  a  range  of  observable  characteristics,  there  remains  the  concern  that  there  are
32:1352:85978:22:22:70:541:518:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:unobservables that may be biasing our estimates. For example, if ethnic groups have a persistent
32:1353:86074:22:22:70:541:496:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:unobservable propensity to engage in conflict and if this affected whether ethnic groups adopted
32:1354:86170:22:22:70:541:474:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a segmentary lineage form of social organization in the past, then this unobservable trait could
32:1355:86266:22:22:70:541:452:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:bias our estimates of interest.  In this case, we would observe a relationship between segmentary
32:1356:86363:22:21:70:541:430:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage systems and conflict today even if no causal relationship exists. These unobservable traits
32:1357:86462:21:22:70:541:409:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:could originate from a range of different sources, including the physical environment or historical
32:1358:86561:22:22:70:541:387:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:experiences. Similarly, there may be unobservable contemporary factors, like the extent to which
32:1359:86657:22:22:70:541:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  rule  of  law  is  able  to  reach  more  remote  locations  from  the  capital  city  or  the  quality  of
32:1360:86769:22:22:70:541:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:transportation and communication infrastructure.  These, and similar factors, might have direct
32:1361:86864:22:22:70:157:321:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:effects on conflict.
32:1362:86884:22:22:85:541:299:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Given this possibility, we also implement an alternative estimation strategy. Since unobservable
32:1363:86980:22:22:70:541:277:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:factors  are,  by  definition,  unobservable,  the  strategy  we  undertake  is  to  examine  and  compare
32:1364:87086:22:22:70:541:255:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:locations  that  are  geographically  close,  but  where  one  location  is  inhabited  by  a  segmentary
32:1365:87191:22:22:70:541:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  society  and  the  other  by  a  society  without  segmentary  lineages.   For  this  analysis,  a
32:1366:87298:22:22:70:541:211:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:10km-by-10km  grid-cell  is  the  unit  of  observation  and  the  sample  consists  of  grid-cells  within
32:1367:87405:22:22:70:541:189:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:pairs  of  contiguous  ethnic  groups  where  one  ethnicity  has  segmentary  lineages  and  the  other
32:1368:87509:22:19:70:541:167:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:does not. Figure5illustrates this setup, showing grid-cells and pairs of contiguous ethnic groups,
32:1369:87607:19:14:79:541:148:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:27The estimated relationships between either population density, night lights, or Islam and conflict are opposite in
32:1370:87723:14:11:70:541:134:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:sign  from  what  one  might  have  expected.   Night  lights  and  population  density  are  both  positively  correlated  with
32:1371:87851:11:11:70:541:123:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:conflict and Islam is negatively correlated.  One explanation for the population-density relationship is that one needs
32:1372:87970:11:11:70:541:112:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:people to fight and thus conflicts often occur where there are people.  In addition,  it may be that places with more
32:1373:88087:11:11:70:541:101:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:populations or higher incomes (proxied by night lights) are more likely to be strategic locations that are the focus of
32:1374:88206:11:11:70:541:90:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:civil conflicts.  Lastly, higher population density may indicate greater population pressures which has been shown to
32:1375:88323:11:0:70:455:79:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:correlate with conflict (e.g., Andre and Platteau,1998, Acemoglu, Fergusson and Johnson,2017).

33:2307:91446:30:13:70:541:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure5:An  illustration  of  the  RD  setting:   an  example  of  ethnicity  pairs,  deadly  conflict
33:2308:91548:13:14:70:541:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:incidents,  and10km  grid-cells.   The  two  segmentary  lineage  ethnic  groups  shown  are  Ambo

33:2310:91738:14:46:70:266:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Nkole (bottom) (all in Western Uganda).
33:2311:91777:46:22:70:541:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:one of which has segmentary lineages and the other does not. The figure also shows the locations
33:2312:91873:22:22:70:204:269:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of deadly conflict incidents.
33:2313:91902:22:22:85:541:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our  strategy  is  to  use  a  regression  discontinuity  (RD)  estimation  method  that  restricts  the
33:2314:92006:22:22:70:541:225:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sample to grid-cells that are sufficiently close to the ethnic boundaries and estimates the causal
33:2315:92104:22:22:70:541:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:effect of segmentary lineage organization on conflict using the estimated difference in conflict at
33:2316:92203:22:22:70:541:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the ethnic boundary.  The benefit of this strategy is that it accounts for unobservable factors that
33:2317:92303:22:22:70:541:159:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:vary smoothly across space.  Therefore, as long as the determinants of unobservable traits – like
33:2318:92400:22:22:70:541:137:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:geography,  history,  idiosyncratic  shocks,  state  presence etc.  –  vary  smoothly,  the  unobservable
33:2319:92505:22:22:70:296:115:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:traits will be accounted for by the RD strategy.
33:2320:92553:22:33:85:348:93:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our RD estimating equation takes the following form:
33:2321:92605:33:0:202:541:60:11:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f4:A:yip=ωp+γISLe(i)+f(locationip) +Z′iΓ+εip(2)
34:2322:92649:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whereiindexes  a10-kilometer  grid-cell,eethnicities  (80in  total),  andpethnicity  pairs  where
34:2323:92746:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:one ethnic group has segmentary lineages and the other does not (68in total).yipis a measure
34:2324:92838:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the extent of conflict in grid-celliwhich is within ethnicity pairp.ISLe(i)is an indicator variable
34:2325:92940:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that equals one if cellibelongs to the ancestral homeland of an ethnic groupethat traditionally
34:2326:93035:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:had  a  segmentary  lineage  organization.f(locationip)denotes  a  polynomial  that  controls  for  a
34:2327:93136:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:smooth function of the geographic location of grid cells.  In our baseline specification, we use a
34:2328:93234:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:location’s Euclidian distance from the border as the running variable, and, following Gelman and
34:2329:93330:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Imbens (2014), use a local linear specification, estimated separately on both sides of the border.
34:2330:93428:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We also report estimates using several other functional forms.ωpdenotes fixed effects for each
34:2331:93522:21:22:70:540:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ethnicity-pair.  The vectorZ′denotes a vector of covariates that includes country fixed effects, as
34:2332:93622:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:well as the following set of grid-cell level geographical controls: elevation, agricultural suitability,
34:2333:93726:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and an indicator if the grid-cell is intersected by a national border.28The sample includes all grid
34:2334:93826:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cells  of  all  pairs  of  ethnic  groups  that  share  a  border  and  where  one  has  segmentary  lineages
34:2335:93935:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and the other does not.29The sample is further restricted to grid-cells that are within a certain
34:2336:94032:22:22:70:457:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:distance of the border of the two ethnic groups, either60,80, or100kilometers.
34:2337:94110:22:22:85:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Before  turning  to  our  estimates  we  first  examine  the  raw  data  for  the  RD  sample.   Figures
34:2338:94214:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:6a–6d show  a bin scatterplots (with20bins)  of  the unconditional relationship between  each  of
34:2339:94311:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the four types of conflict and the distance from the ethnicity boundary.  Even in the raw data, a
34:2340:94408:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:discontinuity at the border is apparent.  We observe a discontinuous increase in conflict on the
34:2341:94504:22:22:70:489:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage side of the border. We next turn to our more formal RD estimates.
34:2342:94588:22:22:85:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Estimates  of  equation  (2),  for  each  of  our  three  conflict  measures  (incidents,  deaths,  and
34:2343:94691:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:months),  are  reported  in  Table4.   For  each  outcome,  we  report  three  specifications,  each  in  a
34:2344:94798:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:different column.  In the first, we only include ethnicity pair fixed effects; in the second, we add
34:2345:94898:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:country fixed effects; and in the third, we add the set of geographic controls.  Each panel of the
34:2346:94996:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:table reports estimates for a different type of conflict, either all conflicts, civil conflict, non-civil
34:2347:95101:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflicts,  and  within-group  conflicts.   All  estimates  use  a  restricted  sample  of  grid  cells  within
34:2348:95212:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:60km  of  the  ethnicity-pair  border.   We  find  that  in  every  specification,  and  irrespective  of  the
34:2349:95322:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:measure of conflict, the estimated effect of segmentary lineage systems on conflict is positive and
34:2350:95421:22:23:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:statistically significant. We also find that for each outcome, the magnitude of the estimated effect
34:2351:95521:23:13:79:415:87:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:28Details, including sources of these measures, are provided in the online appendix.
34:2352:95605:13:14:79:541:74:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:29If an ethnic group is adjacent to more than one ethnic group of different treatment status, then the ethnic group
34:2353:95720:14:0:70:193:60:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:can be a part of multiple pairs.

37:2427:100596:14:14:70:541:221:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:correlation  plots  (20bins)  from  the  specification  that  conditions  on  ethnicity-pair  fixed  effects
37:2428:100704:14:13:70:541:207:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and country fixed effects.  They-axis reports the natural log of one plus the number of deadly
37:2429:100798:13:14:70:540:194:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict incidents for each of the the four different types of conflict.  Thex-axis reports distance
37:2430:100898:14:13:70:541:180:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(in kilometers) from the borders between segmentary lineage and non-segmentary lineage soci-
37:2431:100990:13:14:70:541:167:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:eties.   The  border  is  at  kilometer  0,  and  positive  values  indicate  kilometers  in  the  territories  of
37:2432:101104:14:0:70:211:153:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage societies.
38:2433:101135:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:This is particularly important since, in reality, one may not observe clear borders between ethnic
38:2434:101233:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups, and instead only a gradual change of the mix of ethnicities over space. Therefore, we now
38:2435:101330:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:check the validity of our use Murdock’s ethnic boundaries by examining how self-reported ethnic
38:2436:101425:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:affiliation  varies  at  ethnicity  boundaries.   For  this,  we  use  round3of  theAfrobarometersurvey,
38:2437:101529:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:which records the self-reported ethnicity of respondents, as well as their location, which has been
38:2438:101628:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:geo-referenced by Nunn and Wantchekon (2011).  Combining this information with the ethnicity
38:2439:101720:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:map from Murdock (1959), we are able to examine whether we observe a discontinuity in ethnic
38:2440:101812:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:identity at the Murdock boundaries among our sample of ethnicity pairs. This is shown in Figure
38:2441:101907:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:8, which reports the bivariate relationship between distance from the border and ethnic affiliation.
38:2442:102007:21:22:70:540:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:They-axis displays the fraction of the population in a bin that reports that they are a member
38:2443:102101:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of a segmentary lineage society and thex-axis is distance in kilometers from the border, with a
38:2444:102196:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:positive distance indicating a location within the territory of the segmentary lineage society and
38:2445:102294:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a negative distance indicating a location outside of the segmentary lineage territory. We find that
38:2446:102393:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:there is a discontinuous change in the fraction of the population that report that they are members
38:2447:102492:22:22:70:304:417:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:of a segmentary lineage society at the borders.30
38:2448:102541:22:22:85:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The estimates from Figure8have important implications for assessing the relative magnitudes
38:2449:102632:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  the  estimate  OLS  and  RD  effects.   According  to  the  estimated  RD  coefficients,  segmentary
38:2450:102736:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  organization  is  associated  with  an  increase  in  conflict  of  0.082  to  0.104  standard  devia-
38:2451:102847:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tions.31These estimates are smaller than those from the cross-ethnicity OLS regressions (reported
38:2452:102944:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in Table3).  According to the OLS estimates, segmentary lineage organization is associated with
38:2453:103039:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an  increase  in  conflict  of  0.333  to  0.622  standard  deviations.   Thus,  the  magnitude  of  the  OLS
38:2454:103148:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates  are  significantly  larger  than  the  RD  estimates.   Although  one  explanation  for  this  is
38:2455:103256:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a  potential  bias  from  unobservables  present  in  the  OLS  estimates,  the  difference  might  also  be
38:2456:103364:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:explained  by  the  fact  that  close  to  the  border  within  a  segmentary  lineage  society,  a  smaller
38:2457:103472:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fraction of the population is likely to belong to the segmentary lineage society. As shown in Figure
38:2458:103572:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:8,  close to the border approximately50% of the population does not belong to the segmentary
38:2459:103664:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage group. This, suggests that the magnitude of the RD estimates could be biased downwards
38:2460:103758:22:19:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by this amount as well. In addition, if conflict in non-segmentary lineage ethnic groups is affected
38:2461:103858:19:15:79:541:113:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:30In Appendix Figure A3, we report RD plots for pairs of prominent ethnic groups that have been widely studied
38:2462:103968:15:11:70:541:98:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:in the anthropology literature:  Ganda and Soga, and Sotho and Zulu.  In both cases, we observe a discontinuous and
38:2463:104083:11:9:70:383:87:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:sharp change in self-reported ethnicity at Murdock’s ethnic group boundaries.
38:2464:104160:9:0:79:310:78:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:31See Appendix Tables A1and A9for summary statistics.

39:2466:104329:41:14:70:541:468:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure8:    This  graph  presents  the  relationship  between  self-reported  ethnicity  and  geographic
39:2467:104433:14:13:70:541:454:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:location  based  on  survey  data  from  Round3of  theAfrobarometerSurvey.   Data  are  aggregated
39:2468:104531:13:14:70:541:441:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for all borders between segmentary lineage and non-segmentary lineage societies in our sample.
39:2469:104625:14:13:70:541:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Thex-axis reports geographic distance.  Positive values imply kilometers into the territory of the
39:2470:104723:13:14:70:541:414:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage society and negative values are kilometers into the non-segmentary lineage

39:2473:104957:47:22:70:541:340:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by  nearby  segmentary  lineage  groups,  then  this  spillover  to  the  control  group  will  cause  the
39:2474:105063:22:39:70:282:318:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimated effects at the border to be muted.
39:2475:105107:39:29:70:257:279:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:B.  Robustness and Sensitivity Checks
39:2476:105144:29:22:70:541:250:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We  now  check  the  sensitivity  of  our  estimates  to  a  range  of  robustness  checks,  which  include:
39:2477:105252:22:22:70:541:228:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:alternative  specifications  for  the  running  variable,  different  restrictions  on  the  window  of  ob-
39:2478:105360:22:22:70:541:206:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:servations  that  are  included  in  the  sample,  and  estimation  using  Poisson  or  negative  binomial
39:2479:105466:22:22:70:541:184:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:models.    The  estimates  are  reported  in  Table5,  where  each  column  reports  estimates  using
39:2480:105567:22:22:70:540:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a  different  restriction  on  the  range  of  observations  included  in  the  sample  (60km,80km,  or
39:2481:105670:22:22:70:541:140:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:100km),  and  each  panel  reports  different  running  variables  and  estimators.32In  panel  A,  for
39:2482:105773:22:22:70:541:118:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:reference, we report the baseline estimates from Table4.  In panels B and C, we use the baseline
39:2483:105869:22:19:70:541:96:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:running variable, but use a negative binomial and Poisson estimator.  In panels D to I, we report
39:2484:105966:19:14:79:541:77:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:32The estimates are for total conflicts. The estimates for civil conflicts, non-civil conflicts, and within-group conflicts
39:2485:106089:14:0:70:150:63:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:are similarly robust.
40:2486:106112:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates using more flexible specifications for the running variable.  Specifically, we use latitude
40:2487:106213:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  longitude  (and  their  interaction)  instead  of  Euclidean  distance  as  running  variables.   This
40:2488:106320:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:allows us to control more directly for features that vary over two-dimensional space rather than
40:2489:106416:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:collapsing a two-dimensional location into a one-dimensional distance measure (see Dell (2010)
40:2490:106510:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:for a similar strategy).  In panel D, we include the baseline running variable interacted with14
40:2491:106606:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cluster indicator variables, where a cluster is defined as a set of contiguous ethnic groups.  Thus,
40:2492:106706:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in this specification, the coefficient on the running variable is allowed to differ for different ethnic
40:2493:106810:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups  in  the  same  region.   In  panel  E,  rather  than  using  the  distance  from  the  border  as  the
40:2494:106920:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:running variable,  we use latitude and longitude and interact both with the14cluster indicator
40:2495:107014:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variables. In panel F, we include quadratic polynomials in the latitude and longitude (i.e. latitude,
40:2496:107115:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:longitude,  squared,  longitude  squared,  and  latitude  times  longitude),  with  each  component  of
40:2497:107218:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the polynomial interacted with the14cluster indicators. Panels G–I are equivalent to panels D–F,
40:2498:107314:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:except instead of interacting distance or latitude and longitude with14cluster indicator variables,
40:2499:107413:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we interact them with68pair indicator variables.  Although these are demanding specifications
40:2500:107506:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(the running variable in Panel I, for example, consists of340variables) by allowing the running
40:2501:107601:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variable to vary for each ethnicity pair we are about to control for specific conflict patterns around
40:2502:107703:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:each  border  segment.   Overall,  the  estimates  using  any  of  these  alternative  specifications  are
40:2503:107809:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:similar to the baseline RD estimates. The estimated coefficients all remain positive and similar in
40:2504:107908:22:22:70:462:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:magnitude, and in nearly every specification they remain statistically significant.
40:2505:107991:22:22:85:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  final  robustness  check  that  we  perform  concerns  the  precision  of  the  location  data  for
40:2506:108095:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflicts.  This is particularly important for the RD estimates since they are derived from differ-
40:2507:108194:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ences in conflict intensity between areas that are geographically close.  As a result, misreported
40:2508:108292:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict locations and imprecise geocoding of the conflict data could potentially bias the results.
40:2509:108391:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To confront this issue, we re-estimate equation (2), reporting the same specifications as in Table
40:2510:108489:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:4,  except  that  we  exclude  conflict  incidents  that,  according  to  the  ACLED  documentation,  are
40:2511:108594:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:georeferenced with lower precision.33While conflict incidents are only included in the ACLED
40:2512:108686:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:data  if  a  minimum  level  of  information  about  geographic  location  is  known,  it  is  nevertheless
40:2513:108793:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:important that our results are robust when we restrict to conflict incidents that are georeferenced
40:2514:108892:22:23:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with a high level of certainty.  The estimates, which are reported in Appendix Table A10, show
40:2515:108986:23:15:79:541:87:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:33We exclude conflicts that are given a score of3in ACLED’s geo-precision measure. These conflicts make up4.75%
40:2516:109097:15:0:70:251:72:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:of the all observations in the ACLED dataset.
41:2517:109144:0:39:70:438:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that our estimates are nearly identical when these observations are omitted.
41:2518:109220:39:29:70:375:685:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:C.  Checking Smoothness of Observables at Ethnic Boundaries
41:2519:109279:29:22:70:541:656:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:One  assumption  of  the  RD  approach  is  that  unobservables  vary  smoothly  across  the  borders.
41:2520:109381:22:22:70:541:634:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Although this is impossible to test directly, we glean evidence about the validity of this assump-
41:2521:109479:22:22:70:541:612:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tion  by  estimating  whether  there  appears  to  be  a  discontinuity  at  the  border  for  the  following
41:2522:109588:22:22:70:541:590:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:observable  variables:   elevation,  slope,  average  temperature,  the  presence  of  a  body  of  water,
41:2523:109694:22:22:70:541:568:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:suitability for the cultivation of cereals,34the percentage of land that is currently under cultivation,
41:2524:109798:22:22:70:541:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the presence of petroleum, the presence of diamonds, the number of mission stations during the
41:2525:109892:22:22:70:541:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:early colonial period, an indicator for the presence of a colonial railway, and an indicator for the
41:2526:109992:22:22:70:540:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:presence of a pre-colonial explorer route.35We check for discontinuities by estimating equation
41:2527:110087:22:44:70:541:480:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(2) with each variable as the dependent variable. Table6reports estimates using the specification
41:2528:110288:44:21:70:541:436:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  indicator  is  always  small  in  magnitude  and  it  is  never  statistically  different  from  zero.
41:2529:110399:21:22:70:541:415:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Appendix Figure A3reports the RD plots, which show no sign of the type of discontinuities that
41:2530:110493:22:22:70:541:393:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we  find  for  segmentary  lineage  organization.   Therefore,  the  estimates  reduce  the  concern  that
41:2531:110599:22:39:70:517:371:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:other factors may also vary discontinuously at the borders that are used in our RD analysis.
41:2532:110691:39:29:70:361:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:D.  Placebo RD Estimates: Do Other Traits Affect Conflict?
41:2533:110749:29:22:70:541:303:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Although we find no evidence of discontinuities in geographic or historical factors, there remains
41:2534:110847:22:22:70:541:281:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the concern that other ethnic characteristics, besides segmentary lineage organization, may also
41:2535:110943:22:22:70:541:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:vary discontinuously at the boundaries.  To threaten the validity of our RD estimates, any other
41:2536:111039:22:22:70:541:237:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ethnic  differences  must  have  an  independent  effect  on  contemporary  conflict.   If  this  were  the
41:2537:111146:22:22:70:541:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:case, and if segmentary lineage organization were correlated with the other characteristics, then
41:2538:111243:22:22:70:322:193:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the effects we estimate might really be due to these.
41:2539:111296:22:22:85:541:171:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:To check for this possibility,  we conduct a  series of ‘placebo’ estimates where  we undertake
41:2540:111391:22:22:70:541:149:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the same procedure as for our baseline RD estimates except that ethnicity pairs are created, and
41:2541:111487:22:22:70:541:127:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:treatment and control defined, using ethnicity characteristics other than segmentary lineage.  We
41:2542:111584:22:19:70:541:105:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:then re-estimate equation (2) to obtain estimates of the impact of the characteristic on conflict. To
41:2543:111685:19:14:79:541:86:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:34Cereals include: wheat, wetland rice, dryland rice, maize, barley, rye, pearl millet, foxtail millet, sorghum, oat, and
41:2544:111806:14:10:70:116:72:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:buckwheat.
41:2545:111816:10:0:79:343:62:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:35See the paper’s online appendix for the details of each measure.

45:2709:123919:0:34:70:154:724:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:C:6.  Mechanisms
45:2710:123933:34:29:70:186:690:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:A.  Onset and Duration
45:2711:123955:29:22:70:541:661:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To  this  point,  our  OLS  and  RD  estimates  suggest  that  segmentary  lineage  organization  is  as-
45:2712:124060:22:22:70:541:639:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sociated  with  more  conflict.   This  could  be  either  because  segmentary  lineages  cause  existing
45:2713:124165:22:22:70:541:617:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflicts  to  escalate  and  last  longer  (i.e.,  longer  duration)  or  because  they  result  in  more  new
45:2714:124276:22:22:70:541:595:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflicts (i.e., more onset) or a combination of the two. In theory, the effect of segmentary lineage
45:2715:124377:22:22:70:541:573:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization on these two channels could be very different.  For example, if segmentary lineage
45:2716:124472:22:22:70:541:551:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization causes conflicts to escalate, as case-study evidence suggests, one could imagine that
45:2717:124570:22:22:70:541:529:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:this  is  foreseen  and  prevents  conflicts  from  starting  in  the  first  place.38That  is,  the  effects  of
45:2718:124683:22:22:70:541:507:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage organization on conflict duration and conflict onset could differ substantially.
45:2719:124782:22:22:85:541:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:To investigate these and related issues, we separately estimate the effects of segmentary lineage
45:2720:124879:22:22:70:541:463:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization on conflict duration and conflict onset. We do this using discrete-time logistic hazard
45:2721:124979:22:33:70:353:441:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:models.39The estimating equation for conflict duration is:
45:2722:125037:33:0:195:210:408:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:log

45:2728:125096:32:22:70:540:376:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:whereeindexes ethnic groups,iepisodes of conflict,  andtyears into the episode of conflict.40
45:2729:125189:22:22:70:541:354:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The sample includes all episodes of conflict – i.e., years and ethnic groups that are ‘at risk’ of a

45:2734:125626:32:0:197:212:235:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:log

45:2743:125984:20:14:79:541:141:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:38Nisbett  and  Cohen  (1996)  make  such  an  argument  when  discussing  the  culture  of  honor  in  the  U.S.  South.
45:2744:126105:14:11:70:541:127:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:These  dynamics  are  able  to  explain  the  simultaneous  presence  of  a  culture  of  honor  and  aggression,  as  well  as  the
45:2745:126237:11:11:70:541:116:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:Southern Gentleman in the U.S. South. Along similar lines, (Ahmed,2013b, pp.21–24) argues that segmentary lineage
45:2746:126350:11:10:70:309:105:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:organization is associated with a form of ‘tribal hospitality’.
45:2747:126413:10:13:79:294:95:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:39See Jenkins (1995) for the finer details of estimation.
45:2748:126470:13:14:79:541:82:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:40The granularity of the ACLED data allows one to measure time in months. However, doing so results in a number
45:2749:126581:14:11:70:541:68:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:of ‘false’ onsets and offsets that are coded anytime there is a pause in fighting of a month or greater, which is common.
45:2750:126702:11:0:70:311:57:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:Thus, we measure time in years rather than something finer.
46:2751:126763:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the episode of peace ends (i.e., conflict onset).  Here too, we assume thathonseti,tfollows a logistic
46:2752:126865:22:22:70:447:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:distribution and we estimateθ(t)using a third-order polynomial in duration.
46:2753:126940:22:22:85:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Estimates  of  equations  (3)  and  (4)  are  reported  in  Table8.   Column1–3report  estimates  of
46:2754:127040:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:equation  (3),  while  columns4–6report  estimates  of  equation  (4).   The  specification  reported
46:2755:127141:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  columns1and4includes  the  third-order  duration  polynomials  only  –  i.e.,ψ(t)andθ(t),
46:2756:127234:22:22:70:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:respectively. In columns2and5, we add country fixed effects, while in columns3and6, we add
46:2757:127324:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our set of geographical and historical controls.  Each panel reports estimates for a different form
46:2758:127423:22:22:70:121:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of conflict.
46:2759:127435:22:21:85:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We  find  strong  evidence  that  segmentary  lineage  organization  is  associated  with  escalation
46:2760:127536:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  conflict.    Specifically,  we  find  a  robust  negative  relationship  between  segmentary  lineage
46:2761:127641:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization and conflict offset.  Once conflicts start, in a segmentary lineage societies, they are
46:2762:127741:22:22:70:301:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:less likely to end and more likely to last longer.
46:2763:127791:22:22:85:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We also find some evidence that segmentary lineage organization is associated with the start
46:2764:127883:22:22:70:541:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  new  conflicts.  We  estimate  a  positive  relationship  between  segmentary  lineage  organization
46:2765:127987:22:22:70:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and conflict onset.  Thus, there is no evidence that segmentary lineage organization reduces the
46:2766:128083:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:probability of conflict onset.  In comparing the onset versus duration/escalation mechanisms, we
46:2767:128179:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:find that the estimated effects on onset tend to be smaller and less precisely estimated than those
46:2768:128278:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for  conflict  offset.   For  example,  in  the  specifications  reported  in  panel  A  of  columns3and6,
46:2769:128384:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the marginal effect (estimated at the mean) of segmentary lineage organization on conflict offset
46:2770:128481:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is about1.71times larger in magnitude than its effect on conflict onset (0.082versus0.048).41In
46:2771:128576:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:addition, two of the three estimates for conflict onset in panel A are not statistically different from
46:2772:128679:22:21:70:94:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:zero.
46:2773:128684:21:22:85:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Overall,  the  estimates  are  consistent  with  the  emphasis  on  an  escalation  channel  that  is
46:2774:128785:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:observed  in  the  ethnographic  literature.   Because  segmentary  lineage  societies  mobilize  a  large
46:2775:128891:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:number of combatants, they have particularly large effects on the duration and scale of conflicts.
46:2776:128989:22:20:70:509:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Once a conflict starts, it is much more likely to escalate and turn into a prolonged conflict.
46:2777:129083:20:14:79:541:156:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:41It is unlikely that this is explained by differences in the relative frequency of onset versus offset.  For all conflicts,
46:2778:129207:14:0:70:134:142:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:they are similar.

47:2822:131841:0:0:271:317:607:58:g_d0_f49:58:g_d0_f49:C:Conflict	Offset
48:2823:131858:0:30:70:187:724:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:B.  The Scale of Conflict
48:2824:131883:30:22:70:541:694:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:As another way of gaining a better understanding of the mechanisms underlying our estimates,
48:2825:131975:22:22:70:541:672:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we examine the effects of segmentary lineage organization on conflicts of different sizes.  Specif-
48:2826:132074:22:22:70:540:650:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ically,  we  use  a  negative  binomial  model  to  estimate  equation  (1)  with  the  number  of  conflict
48:2827:132182:22:21:70:541:628:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:B:incidents  of  each  of  the  following  sizes  as  dependent  variables:  incidents  with0deaths,1-10
48:2828:132284:21:22:70:541:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:deaths,11-100deaths, or100+ deaths. The estimates are reported in Table9.42We find a positive
48:2829:132377:22:22:70:541:585:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relationship  between  segmentary  lineage  and  the  incidence  of  conflict  incidents  of  all  sizes.
48:2830:132482:22:22:70:541:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:However, the magnitude of the coefficient increases monotonically with the scale of the conflict
48:2831:132578:22:22:70:541:541:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as  measured  by  the  number  of  fatalities.   As  shown,  in  panels  A  to  D,  this  is  true  irrespective
48:2832:132690:22:22:70:541:519:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  whether  we  examine  all  conflicts,  civil  conflict,  non-civil  conflict,  or  within-group  conflicts.
48:2833:132801:22:22:70:541:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:This  finding  is  consistent  with  segmentary  lineage  organization  mobilizing  large  numbers  of
48:2834:132903:22:39:70:449:475:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:combatants, which causes small disputes to escalate into larger-scale conflicts.
48:2835:132983:39:29:70:491:436:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f10:C:C.  The Differential Relationship between Adverse Environmental Shocks and Conflict
48:2836:133066:29:22:70:541:407:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The  final  exercise  that  we  undertake  to  better  understand  the  channels  behind  our  findings
48:2837:133169:22:22:70:541:385:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:examines  how  environmental  shocks,  which  have  been  shown  to  cause  conflict,  interact  with
48:2838:133270:22:22:70:541:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  presence  of  segmentary  lineage  systems.It  is  possible  that  segmentary  lineage  groups
48:2839:133369:22:22:70:541:341:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:have a more difficulty dealing with adverse environmental shocks and mitigating the extent to
48:2840:133462:22:22:70:541:319:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:which they lead to escalated armed conflict.  Motivated by this, we test whether adverse rainfall
48:2841:133559:22:22:70:541:297:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:shocks lead to more conflict in segmentary lineage societies compared to non-segmentary lineage
48:2842:133654:22:22:70:541:275:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:societies.   Using  a  monthly  panel  of  ethnic  groups,  we  first  examine  the  relationship  between
48:2843:133760:22:22:70:541:253:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:adverse rainfall shocks and conflict. This is motivated by prior evidence of a relationship between
48:2844:133859:22:21:70:541:231:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rainfall and conflict within sub-Saharan Africa (e.g., Miguel et al.,2004, Rogall,2014).  We then
48:2845:133956:21:22:70:541:210:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:allow the relationship to differ depending on whether the ethnic group has a segmentary lineage
48:2846:134051:22:22:70:541:188:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization or not.  Given that rainfall shocks provide a catalyst for conflict, these estimates test
48:2847:134153:22:22:70:541:166:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  extent  to  which  segmentary  lineages  amplify  the  effects  of  these  shocks,  allowing  them  to
48:2848:134260:22:22:70:280:144:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:more frequently result in full-scale conflict.
48:2849:134306:22:19:85:541:122:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  rainfall  data  are  from  the  Tropical  Rainfall  Measuring  Mission  (TRMM)  satellite.43The
48:2850:134406:19:13:79:495:103:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:42In all specifications, we control for country fixed effects, geographical controls, and historical controls.
48:2851:134516:13:15:79:541:90:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:43The  use  of  satellite  data  is  especially  important  in  our  context  since  ground  sensors  are  scarce.Wherever
48:2852:134638:15:11:70:541:75:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:possible,  TRMM  data  are  also  validated  using  data  from  “ground-based  radar,  rain  gauges  and  disdrometers”:
48:2853:134758:11:0:70:274:64:9:g_d0_f51:9:g_d0_f4:F:https://pmm.nasa.gov/TRMM/ground-validation.

50:2911:138222:22:21:70:541:348:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lags  of  the  dependent  variable,∑6j=1γjyi,t−j.   Given  the  high  frequency  of  our  panel  (which  is
50:2912:138329:21:22:70:541:327:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:monthly),  it  is  important  to  account  for  lagged  conflict.   We  include  all  lags  of  the  dependent
50:2913:138439:22:22:70:541:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variable that are statistically significant, which is six.  The coefficient of interest isβ2.  A positive
50:2914:138544:22:22:70:541:283:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:coefficient suggests that within segmentary lineage societies, adverse rainfall shocks lead to more
50:2915:138643:22:22:70:314:261:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflicts than in non-segmentary lineage societies.

52:2990:143871:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:since the previous literature examining the relationship between rainfall and conflicts has focused
52:2991:143970:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on  civil  wars  (Miguel  et  al.,2004).   The  estimates  also  show  effects  for  within-group  conflicts,

52:2995:144317:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:deviation  increase  in  the  adverse  rainfall  shock  variable,  which  is4.015mm,  leads  to  a0.85%
