52:2998:144592:22:22:85:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In equation (5), because we have included ethnicity fixed effects, we are unable to estimate the
52:2999:144688:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:direct effect of segmentary lineage when there is average rainfall. This is because the uninteracted
52:3000:144788:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage indicator variable is absorbed by the equation’s ethnicity fixed effects. There-
52:3001:144887:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fore,  we also estimate a version of equation (5) that does not include the ethnicity fixed effects
52:3002:144986:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(or  their  interactions  with  a  time  trend),  but  instead  includes  the  segmentary  lineage  indicator
52:3003:145095:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variable, as well as our baseline set of ethnicity-level geographic and historical covariates.  From
52:3004:145195:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the estimates, which are reported in columns3and6segmentary lineage societies are associated
52:3005:145287:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with more conflict even when rainfall is at its historical average (Neg Shocki,t=0).  The estimated
52:3006:145386:21:22:70:541:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:effect,  which  is  given  by  the  coefficient  for  the  (uninteracted)  segmentary  lineage  indicator
52:3007:145491:22:22:70:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variable,  is  positive,  sizeable,  and  statistically  significant.   This  is  consistent  with  other  factors,
52:3008:145606:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:besides  adverse  rainfall,  being  a  catalyst  for  conflict,  which  is  then  exacerbated  by  segmentary
52:3009:145715:22:22:70:172:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage organization.
52:3010:145736:22:22:85:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We  also  check  the  robustness  of  these  findings  to  the  use  of  alternative  specifications  that
52:3011:145842:22:19:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:have been used in previous studies that examine the effects of weather shocks on conflict.  These
52:3012:145939:19:15:79:541:113:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:47Given the presence of lagged dependent variables in our regression equation, there is concerned about the presence
52:3013:146055:15:11:70:541:98:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:of a Nickel bias.  If we instead use an Arellano-Bond estimator, we obtain very similar results to what we report here.
52:3014:146174:11:11:70:541:87:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:The coefficient on the interaction term in column2of Panel A, for example, is 2.602 and significant at the5% level.
52:3015:146289:11:11:70:541:76:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:Also, as we report in Appendix Table A12, we obtain similar estimates using specifications that do not include lags of
52:3016:146407:11:0:70:164:65:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:the dependent variable.
53:3017:146432:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates are reported in Appendix Table A12.  Specifically,  we report estimates of a version of
53:3018:146529:22:22:70:540:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:equation (5) without lagged dependent variables, but with:  ethnicity fixed effects and ethnicity-
53:3019:146627:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:specific  linear  time  trends  (panel  A);48ethnicity  fixed  effects  and  time  fixed  effects  (panel  B);
53:3020:146737:22:40:70:481:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ethnicity fixed effects, time fixed effects, and ethnicity-specific time trends (panel C).
53:3021:146827:40:34:70:353:618:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:C:7.  Discussion of Implications and External Validity
53:3022:146879:34:22:70:541:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We feel that our findings provide insight into a previously unexplored determinant of conflict.
53:3023:146974:22:22:70:541:562:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Although  our  findings  hold  for  all  forms  of  conflict,  they  are  potentially  the  most  informative
53:3024:147083:22:22:70:541:540:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for civil conflicts,  helping us to better understand why some armed non-state actors have been
53:3025:147178:22:22:70:541:518:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:better  able  to  recruit  soldiers  than  others.   As  an  example  of  a  non-state  organization  that  has
53:3026:147289:22:22:70:541:496:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:been successful in this dimension consider Boko Haram in Northern Nigeria.  It is very difficult
53:3027:147385:22:22:70:541:474:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to explain their success using standard determinants. Certainly, the Nigerian state lacks capacity,
53:3028:147484:22:22:70:541:452:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:but it does so everywhere, not just in the North. Indubitably, there is greed in Nigeria and perhaps
53:3029:147584:22:21:70:541:430:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the incentive to mobilize is due to the prospect of grabbing oil rents.  But the oil is in the South,
53:3030:147685:21:22:70:541:409:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not in the North.  Certainly, the North also has legitimate grievances,  but one can imagine that
53:3031:147782:22:22:70:541:387:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:such grievances are widespread in Nigeria.  Why then has the rebellion in the North attracted so
53:3032:147878:22:22:70:150:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:many followers?
53:3033:147893:22:22:85:541:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our findings suggest that one missing element in such a puzzle may be the social structure of
53:3034:147986:22:22:70:541:321:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the societies involved.  Boko Haram has recruited primarily from the Kanuri people who histor-
53:3035:148080:22:22:70:541:299:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ically constituted a segmentary lineage society.  That there is a connection between segmentary
53:3036:148175:22:22:70:541:277:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  societies  and  Boko  Haram  has  been  argued  by  Akbar  Ahmed  (2013b)  who  argues  that
53:3037:148276:22:31:70:451:255:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:they actively recruit where segmentary lineage structures are most prominent:
53:3038:148353:31:22:114:514:224:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:“Over the previous three years,  the group popularly known as Boko Haram had
53:3039:148429:22:22:98:514:202:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:struck fear into Nigerians with its ferocious attacks on both government and civilian
53:3040:148514:22:22:98:514:180:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:targets. . . The  group  was  dominated  by  the  historically  segmentary  lineage  Kanuri
53:3041:148605:22:22:98:514:158:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:people,  who  previously  had  their  own  independent  kingdom  until  British  colonial-
53:3042:148695:22:21:98:514:136:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:ism. . . [Later],  the  group  began  to  recruit  other  ethnic  groups,  such  as  the  Fulani,
53:3043:148792:21:20:98:514:115:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:another segmentary lineage people in northern Nigeria.  The first suicide bomber in
53:3044:148875:20:0:79:458:95:7:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f4:F:48This is similar to the specification from Burke, Miguel, Satyanath, Dykema and Lobell (2009).
54:3045:148972:0:22:98:514:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Nigerian  history,  who  Boko  Haram  announced  was  Fulani,  blew  himself  up  in  the
54:3046:149061:22:26:98:467:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:national police headquarters in Abuja in June2011” (Ahmed,2013b, p.129).
54:3047:149133:26:22:85:541:676:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Though  we  have  conducted  our  analysis  within  Africa  because  of  the  rich  geocoded  sub-
54:3048:149231:22:22:70:541:654:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:national  conflict  data,  the  findings  we  present  are  likely  applicable  beyond  the  continent.   For
54:3049:149340:22:22:70:541:632:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:example, Osama bin Laden and many individuals recruited to Al Qaeda were and are Yemeni;
54:3050:149428:22:22:70:541:610:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:moreover, “Yemeni tribes in Asir are organized around a segmentary lineage system, with elders
54:3051:149522:22:22:70:541:588:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  councils,  a  spirit  of  egalitarianism,  and  a  code  of  honor  guiding  society  that  emphasizes
54:3052:149629:22:22:70:541:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:courage,  loyalty,  hospitality,  and  revenge”  (Ahmed,2013b,  p.110).   The  same  logic  of  lineage-
54:3053:149733:22:22:70:541:544:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:based  obligation  and  revenge  among  segmentary  groups  in  Somalia  and  Sudan  applies  to  the
54:3054:149834:22:22:70:541:522:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Yemeni.  According to Paul Dresch, “If a man from a village in Khamis Abu Dhaybah or Kharif
54:3055:149925:22:22:70:541:500:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:kills  someone  from  Arhab. . . a  debt  exists  between  the  two  tribes. . . a  man’s  immediate  kin  are
54:3056:150035:22:22:70:541:478:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:involved (those who Islamic law recognizes as always al-dam), but men much further from the
54:3057:150126:22:22:70:541:456:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:particular antagonist may also be drawn in.  If a man from section A of our tribe kills someone
54:3058:150221:22:21:70:541:434:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from  another  tribe,  that  other  tribe  might  perhaps  kill  someone  in  a  quite  different  section  of
54:3059:150331:21:22:70:541:413:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ours,  section B” (Dresch,1989,  pp.84–85).  As we documented within Africa,  here too lineage-
54:3060:150426:22:22:70:541:391:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:based obligation and responsibility to participate in conflict appear to facilitate the escalation and
54:3061:150528:22:22:70:541:369:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:persistence of conflicts that otherwise would be small and short-lived.  Thus, it is likely that our
54:3062:150628:22:22:70:284:347:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:findings for Africa also apply more broadly.
54:3063:150672:22:22:85:541:325:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:A better understanding of segmentary lineage systems also has the potential to shed important
54:3064:150765:22:22:70:541:303:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:light and new understanding on key international security issues.  It is possible that segmentary
54:3065:150862:22:22:70:541:281:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage organization is not only associated with within-country conflicts but also with inter-state
54:3066:150961:22:22:70:541:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:warfare,  international  violence,  and  terrorism.   Ahmed  (2013b)  points  out  a  broad  correlation
54:3067:151065:22:22:70:541:237:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:between areas of high-intensity Islamist violence and areas where society is structured based on
54:3068:151161:22:26:70:470:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage organization. In a2013speech, Ahmed claimed the following:
54:3069:151238:26:22:114:514:189:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:“Here is a correlation for you.  Ask yourselves:  where are [US] drones most used?
54:3070:151320:22:22:98:514:167:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:They are really segmentary lineage systems: the Pashtuns in Afghanistan and Pakistan
54:3071:151404:22:22:98:514:145:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:tribal  areas,  mainly  in  Waziristan;  among  the  Somali  segmentary  lineage  system;
54:3072:151493:22:22:98:514:123:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:the  Yemenis’  segmentary  lineage  system;  the  Kurds  in  eastern  Turkey,  segmentary
54:3073:151582:22:22:98:514:101:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:lineage system; the Tuareg in West Africa, segmentary lineage system.  An immediate
54:3074:151665:22:22:98:514:79:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:correlation.  So there is some connection that we can identify. . . Take a look at these
54:3075:151753:22:0:98:514:57:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:mutant  militant  groups  that  are  emerging:   the  TTP  (Tehrik-i-Taliban  Pakistan),  for
55:3076:151848:0:22:98:514:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:example.   Where  is  it  coming  out  of?   It’s  coming  out  of  a  specific  tribe,  a  specific
55:3077:151948:22:22:98:514:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:clan.  Al Shabaab:  tribal.  Tribal:  Boko Haram in West Africa.  Again, because we tend
55:3078:152036:22:22:98:514:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:to jump on Islam as the explanation for what’s going on, we are missing this whole
55:3079:152118:22:22:98:514:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:tribal  basis  of  the  discussion.   All  of  these  are  coming  out  of  straight  segmentary
55:3080:152214:22:31:98:324:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:lineage system backgrounds.” (Ahmed,2013a)
55:3081:152256:31:22:85:541:605:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Philip Salzman extends this reasoning and argues that Islam, at its inception, was structured as
55:3082:152352:22:43:70:541:583:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an amalgamation of segmentary lineage societies and was designed to unite these tribes against
55:3083:152553:43:22:70:541:540:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:extending  the  basic  tribal  principle  of  balanced  opposition.  This  Muhammad  did  by  opposing
55:3084:152655:22:22:70:541:518:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the Muslim to the infidel, and the dar al-Islam, the land of Islam and peace, to the dar al-harb,
55:3085:152752:22:22:70:541:496:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the land of the infidels and conflict.  Balanced opposition was raised to a higher structural level
55:3086:152851:22:22:70:541:474:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and the newly Muslim tribes were unified in the face of the infidel enemy” (Salzman,2007, pp.
55:3087:152944:22:22:70:541:452:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:B:137–138).  In this conceptualization, the entire Islamic world comprises the largest tribal segment
55:3088:153043:22:22:70:541:430:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that is compelled to unite against any non-Muslim – infidels,  the West,  or the dar al-harb.  For
55:3089:153141:22:22:70:541:408:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Salzman,  an  understanding  of  segmentary  organization  becomes  crucial  to  understanding  all
55:3090:153240:22:22:70:177:386:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Islam-fueled violence.
55:3091:153262:22:22:85:541:364:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:This logic is moreover not confined to the writing of academic anthropologists. Philip Zeman,
55:3092:153355:22:22:70:541:342:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a strategist with the U.S. Marine Corps,  has argued that there is a strong relationship between
55:3093:153451:22:22:70:541:320:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary organization and “terror.”  He writes not only that “members of Islamist extremist
55:3094:153544:22:22:70:541:298:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups commonly come from societies with strong tribal [segmentary] traditions” but also that
55:3095:153637:22:21:70:541:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:there are explicit links between tribal organization and violent extremism (Zeman,2009, p.682).
55:3096:153732:21:22:70:541:255:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:For Zeman, there is a national security “need for in-depth understanding of tribal systems and
55:3097:153826:22:22:70:234:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:influences” (Zeman,2009, p.682).
55:3098:153858:22:22:85:541:211:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Although  our  analysis  has  focused  specifically  on  the  African  context,  our  findings  have
55:3099:153958:22:22:70:541:189:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  potential  to  explain  conflict  elsewhere.   They  raise  the  possibility  that  segmentary  lineage
55:3100:154066:22:41:70:333:167:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:organization may be a crucial driver of global conflict.
55:3101:154122:41:33:70:147:126:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:C:8.  Conclusion
55:3102:154136:33:22:70:541:93:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We have tested a long-standing hypothesis from the anthropology literature about the relationship
55:3103:154233:22:0:70:541:71:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:between  segmentary  lineage  organization  and  conflict.   A  rich  ethnographic  literature  suggests
56:3104:154339:0:22:70:541:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that segmentary lineage organization results in large numbers of men being mobilized for warfare
56:3105:154435:22:22:70:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:anytime there is a dispute or conflict.  This is true when the initial feud is between individuals
56:3106:154533:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:within the same segment, but especially when it is between individuals from different segments or
56:3107:154630:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineages. To investigate these ideas, we collected information from existing ethnographic sources
56:3108:154727:22:22:70:406:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on the social structure of145ethnic groups from sub-Saharan Africa.
56:3109:154794:22:22:85:541:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our first strategy was to examine the cross-ethnicity relationship between the historical pres-
56:3110:154889:22:22:70:541:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ence of a segmentary lineage system and measures of conflict today.  Our second empirical strat-
56:3111:154985:22:22:70:541:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:egy was to restrict our analysis to pairs of contiguous ethnic groups where one ethnic group was
56:3112:155081:22:21:70:541:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:traditionally organized based on segmentary lineages and the other was not. Examining variation
56:3113:155176:21:22:70:541:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:across10km-by-10km grid-cells,  we estimated the effect of segmentary lineage organization on
56:3114:155269:22:22:70:541:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflict using a regression discontinuity (RD) approach. This strategy allowed us to better control
56:3115:155368:22:22:70:541:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for any omitted factors that change smoothly over space, such as geographic factors, ecological
56:3116:155463:22:22:70:541:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:characteristics, or historical shocks. Using either strategy, we found a strong positive relationship
56:3117:155564:22:22:70:364:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:between segmentary lineage organization and conflict today.
56:3118:155623:22:22:85:541:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Motivated by the existing case-study and historical literatures, which suggest that the primary
56:3119:155718:22:22:70:541:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:consequence of segmentary lineages is to cause the escalation of conflicts that otherwise would
56:3120:155813:22:22:70:541:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:have been relatively small, we turned to an examination of mechanisms. Estimating hazard mod-
56:3121:155906:22:22:70:541:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:els, we found robust evidence that segmentary lineage organization prolongs conflicts once they
56:3122:156001:22:22:70:541:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:start.  The estimated effects on conflict onset, although positive, were smaller in magnitude and
56:3123:156098:22:22:70:541:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:less robust. We also examined the effects of segmentary lineage organization on the prevalence of
56:3124:156195:22:22:70:541:285:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conflicts of different sizes. We found that although segmentary lineage organization is positively
56:3125:156293:22:21:70:541:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:associated  with  conflicts  of  all  sizes,  the  relationship  was  much  larger  in  magnitude  and  more
56:3126:156401:21:22:70:285:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:precisely estimated for larger-scale conflicts.
56:3127:156448:22:22:85:541:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  final  exercise  that  we  undertook  was  to  examine  the  differential  ability  of  segmentary
56:3128:156551:22:22:70:541:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage and non-segmentary lineage societies to cope with adverse rainfall shocks.  Examining a
56:3129:156646:22:22:70:541:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:monthly panel at the ethnicity-level, we first documented a positive relationship between adverse
56:3130:156743:22:22:70:541:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rainfall  shocks  and  conflict  across  the145ethnic  groups  in  our  sample.   We  then  allowed  the
56:3131:156847:22:22:70:541:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:effect to differ for segmentary lineage and non-segmentary lineage societies and found that the
56:3132:156942:22:22:70:541:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:average effect was being driven solely by segmentary lineage societies.  Among non-segmentary
56:3133:157035:22:22:70:541:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lineage  societies,  there  was  no  relationship  between  adverse  rainfall  shocks  and  conflict.   This
56:3134:157143:22:0:70:541:66:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:suggests that segmentary lineage societies are less successful at containing conflicts that results
57:3135:157244:0:22:70:210:724:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from adverse rainfall shocks.
57:3136:157273:22:22:85:541:702:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Although our analysis has focused specifically on the African context, our results are applica-
57:3137:157368:22:22:70:541:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ble outside of Africa, where segmentary lineage organization is also common. Outside of Africa,
57:3138:157463:22:22:70:541:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  especially  in  the  Middle  East,  there  are  many  examples  of  prolonged  conflicts  involving
57:3139:157567:22:22:70:541:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:groups that are traditionally organized in segmentary lineages.  Thus, our findings suggest that
57:3140:157663:22:50:70:484:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:segmentary lineage organization may be an important determinant of global conflict.
57:3141:157746:50:23:70:130:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:References
